# /start-feature ŌĆö Auto-Setup Feature Development Team

**Feature**: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240)

You are setting up a hybrid agent team for feature development. The PM agent leads the team and owns the ceremony. Your job is minimal setup, then hand control to PM.

---

## Step 1: Create Git Worktree

Slugify the feature description into a branch name:
- Take `feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240)`, lowercase it, replace spaces/special chars with hyphens, truncate to 50 chars
- Prefix with `feature/` (e.g., "add demo mode onboarding" -> `feature/add-demo-mode-onboarding`)

```bash
# Example (adapt the slug from feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240)):
BRANCH_NAME="feature/<slugified-arguments>"
git fetch origin
git worktree add ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} -b ${BRANCH_NAME} origin/main
```

If the worktree or branch already exists, inform the user and ask how to proceed.

Run `pnpm install` in the worktree:
```bash
cd ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} && pnpm install
```

---

## Step 2: Create Named Team

Create the team using TeamCreate. Use the slugified branch name (without `feature/` prefix) as the team name:

```
TeamCreate {
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  description: "Feature team: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240)"
}
```

---

## Step 3: Spawn PM Agent

The PM agent handles scoping, GitHub Issues, and task graph creation. It does NOT spawn other agents ŌĆö only the orchestrator can spawn agents.

```
Task {
  name: "pm-agent",
  subagent_type: "product-manager",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the PM for this feature team.

FEATURE REQUEST: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240)
WORKTREE: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/
BRANCH: feature/<slugified-arguments>
TEAM: feat-<slugified-arguments>

Your responsibilities are scoping, GitHub Issues, task graph, and handoff preparation.
IMPORTANT: You CANNOT spawn agents. Only the orchestrator can. When you need an agent spawned, message the orchestrator with the request.

Follow this protocol:

1. SCOPE: Read docs in docs/ and CLAUDE.md to understand what this feature involves. Check for existing design docs in docs/plans/. Check docs/architecture/ for architecture context. If the scope is unclear, message the orchestrator for clarification.

2. ISSUES: Search for an existing GitHub Issue that matches this feature. If one exists, use it. If not, create one with proper description, acceptance criteria, and T-shirt size. Record the issue number.

3. TASK GRAPH: Create the ceremony tasks using TaskCreate, then set dependencies with TaskUpdate:
   - Task: 'TA: Review architecture alignment' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if internal-only (new components, UI, styling)
   - Task: 'LLM Expert: Design prompt architecture' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if feature doesn't involve LLM calls
   - Task: 'PM: Prepare handoff context in GitHub Issue' (no dependencies, you do this yourself)
   - Task: 'Dev: Read handoff and design docs, prepare questions' (blockedBy: TA + LLM Expert if applicable + PM handoff)
   - Task: 'Dev + TA: Reach consensus on implementation approach' (blockedBy: above) -- SKIP if internal-only
   - Task: 'Dev: Implement feature in worktree' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Dev: Verify feature and create PR' (blockedBy: above) -- includes pre-PR verification protocol
   - Task: 'Review: Triple-layer code review (loops until 0 FIX NOW)' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Post final review summary to GitHub PR' (blockedBy: above)

4. DO YOUR OWN TASK: Work on your handoff task -- prepare context in the GitHub Issue (description, acceptance criteria, relevant doc paths, implementation guidance).

   IMPORTANT ŌĆö Classify the feature scope for Dev's verification protocol:
   - Does it touch UI/visual rendering? ŌåÆ Tag: VISUAL
   - Does it produce output artifacts (images, PDFs, exports)? ŌåÆ Tag: OUTPUT_ARTIFACT
   - Does it add new npm dependencies? ŌåÆ Tag: NEW_DEPS
   - Does it change API endpoints? ŌåÆ Tag: API_CHANGE
   Include these tags in the GitHub Issue so Dev knows which verification tiers apply.

5. REQUEST AGENT SPAWNS: When your handoff task is done, message the orchestrator:
   - If TA is needed: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: ta-agent ŌĆö [brief context]'
   - When dev prerequisites are met: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: dev-agent ŌĆö [brief context including issue number and key details]'
   The orchestrator will spawn the agents and assign tasks.

   SKIP TA if the feature is internal-only (new components, UI fixes, styling, LLM provider additions). In that case, mark the TA task as completed with note 'Skipped -- internal-only change'.

   If the feature involves LLM calls (prompts, model selection, token budgets, structured output):
   - 'SPAWN_REQUEST: llm-expert-agent ŌĆö [brief context about the LLM aspect]'
   The LLM Expert will design the prompt architecture, token budget, and model recommendation before dev implements.

   SKIP LLM Expert if the feature doesn't touch LLM code. Mark the task as completed with note 'Skipped -- no LLM impact'.

6. MONITOR: Check TaskList periodically.
   - When Dev creates a PR, message the orchestrator: 'REVIEW_REQUEST: PR #XX is ready for /start-review'
   - The orchestrator will run /start-review which loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, the orchestrator sends them to Dev. Dev fixes and pushes. Review re-runs automatically.
   - You do NOT need to request additional review rounds ŌĆö the loop is built into /start-review.

7. REPORT: When review converges (0 FIX NOW items) and final summary is posted, message the orchestrator: 'PR #XX for feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240) is ready for founder review and merge.'

IMPORTANT RULES:
- NEVER merge PRs -- founder-only
- NEVER try to spawn agents -- message the orchestrator instead
- All dev work happens in the worktree
- If you need user clarification, message the orchestrator who will ask the user
- You can message existing teammates directly via SendMessage for routine coordination
- Task dependencies enforce ceremony order -- don't skip steps
- PRE-PR GATE (MANDATORY): Before any PR is created, Dev must complete the full verification protocol (see Dev agent instructions). GitHub Actions costs money ŌĆö failed CI runs are wasted spend.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

---

## Step 4: Orchestrator Spawns Agents on PM Request

After PM completes its handoff and sends a SPAWN_REQUEST message, the orchestrator spawns the requested agent:

**For TA (if PM requests it):**
```
Task {
  name: "ta-agent",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the TA for feature team feat-<slugified-arguments>. Feature: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240). Check TaskList for your assigned tasks. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent and later dev-agent. Mark tasks in_progress when starting, completed when done.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the TA task to ta-agent.

**For LLM Expert (if PM requests it):**
```
Task {
  name: "llm-expert-agent",
  subagent_type: "llm-expert",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the LLM Expert for feature team feat-<slugified-arguments>. Feature: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240). Check TaskList for your assigned tasks. Design the prompt architecture, token budget, model recommendation, and output schema for the LLM aspects of this feature. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent and ta-agent. Mark tasks in_progress when starting, completed when done.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the LLM Expert task to llm-expert-agent.

**For Dev (when PM requests it):**
```
Task {
  name: "dev-agent",
  subagent_type: "engineer",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the Dev for feature team feat-<slugified-arguments>. Feature: feat: `insights` CLI command with --native, --hook, --force modes (GitHub Issue #240). Worktree: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/. All code work happens in the worktree. Check TaskList for your tasks. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent. Mark tasks in_progress/completed.

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root ŌĆö must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ ŌĆö must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server ŌĆö do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary
[What this PR does]

## Dependency Audit (if NEW_DEPS)
[Library name]: [Known limitations found, or 'No significant limitations found']

## Verification
- Build: PASS
- Tests: PASS
- [Screenshot of feature rendering] (if VISUAL)
- [Screenshot/proof of output artifact] (if OUTPUT_ARTIFACT)
- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

## During Review Rounds

If the review team sends back FIX NOW items:
1. Read each item carefully
2. Implement the fixes in the worktree
3. Re-run applicable verification tiers (at minimum Tier 1)
4. If fixes are visual, re-capture screenshots
5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable ŌĆö thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

---

## Step 5: Supervise

After spawning agents, your role is active supervisor:

1. **PM handles scoping and task graph** ŌĆö orchestrator handles all agent spawning
2. **Spawn agents when PM sends SPAWN_REQUEST messages**
3. **Intervene when**:
   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user
   - An agent is stuck or reports a blocker -> help unblock
   - PM sends a REVIEW_REQUEST -> run `/start-review` on the PR number
4. **Review loop management**:
   - `/start-review` handles the loop internally (runs rounds until 0 FIX NOW items)
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, relay them to the dev-agent via SendMessage
   - After dev pushes fixes, `/start-review` re-runs targeted reviewers automatically
   - If review hits max rounds (4) without converging, escalate to user
5. **When PM reports "ready for merge"** -> inform the user

---

## Step 6: Cleanup (After PR Merge)

After the founder merges the PR:

1. Send shutdown requests to all teammates (pm-agent, ta-agent, dev-agent)
2. Delete the team: `TeamDelete`
3. Clean up worktree:
```bash
git worktree remove ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>
```
4. Confirm cleanup is complete

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** ŌĆö sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** ŌĆö it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** ŌĆö spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** ŌĆö agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes ŌĆö PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** ŌĆö build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** ŌĆö orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** ŌĆö dev agent must kill any server it starts

# /start-review ŌĆö Triple-Layer Code Review Team

**PR**: 247

You are setting up a triple-layer code review for PR `247`. This can be used standalone or as part of a `/start-feature` team workflow. The review loops until all FIX NOW items are resolved ŌĆö it does NOT end after a single pass.

---

## Step 1: Get PR Details

Fetch the PR details:

```bash
# Get the correct owner from git remote
git remote get-url origin | sed 's/.*[:/]\([^/]*\)\/[^/]*\.git/\1/'
```

Use `gh pr view 247` to get PR title, description, and diff stats.
Use `gh pr diff 247` to get the diff.

Determine the PR scope:
- Count files changed and lines changed per file
- Identify if it touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema, server API)
- Classify changed files into domains for specialist selection (Step 2)

---

## Step 2: Select Domain Specialists

Instead of fixed generalist reviewers, select 1-2 **domain specialists** based on what the PR actually changes. Each specialist combines deep domain expertise with general engineering awareness. See `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the full specialist registry and prompt templates.

### Domain Classification

Classify each changed file into a domain based on file patterns:

| Domain | File Pattern Triggers |
|--------|----------------------|
| **SQL/Database** | `server/src/routes/*.ts` (when containing SQL keywords), `cli/src/db/*.ts` |
| **React/Frontend** | `dashboard/src/**/*.tsx`, `dashboard/src/**/*.ts` |
| **Node/CLI** | `cli/src/commands/*.ts`, `cli/src/utils/*.ts`, `server/src/*.ts` (non-route, non-LLM) |
| **Parser/Provider** | `cli/src/providers/**/*.ts`, `cli/src/parser/*.ts` |
| **LLM** | `server/src/llm/**/*.ts` ŌĆö handled by LLM Expert (separate, unchanged) |

Files that don't match any domain (e.g., `package.json`, `tsconfig.json`, `.gitignore`, `CLAUDE.md`) are ignored during classification.

### Selection Algorithm

1. For each domain, sum the lines changed across all files in that domain
2. **Primary specialist** = domain with the most lines changed
3. **Secondary specialist** = next domain IF it has >= 30% of total changed lines AND is a different domain
4. Cap at **2 domain specialists** (LLM Expert is a separate conditional reviewer)
5. If a PR changes ONLY non-domain files, use the **Node/CLI Specialist** as general-purpose

### LLM Expert (Conditional ŌĆö Unchanged)

**Invoke LLM Expert if ANY of these apply:**
- PR touches `server/src/llm/` (prompts, providers, export-prompts)
- PR adds or modifies LLM API calls
- PR changes structured output schemas or SSE streaming
- PR modifies token budgets or model selection logic
- PR adds new LLM-powered features

**Skip LLM Expert if ALL of these apply:**
- No LLM code touched
- Pure UI, CLI, or schema changes
- Provider (source tool) implementations only

---

## Step 2.5: Pre-Review Gates

Before launching reviewers, check these gates. If any gate fails, the review CANNOT proceed ŌĆö send the PR back to the dev agent (or inform the user if standalone) with what's missing.

### Gate A: New Dependency Audit

Check if `package.json` (any workspace) was modified in the PR diff.

If new dependencies were added:

```
Task {
  name: "dep-auditor",
  subagent_type: "Explore",
  prompt: "Research the following new npm dependencies added in PR #247. For EACH dependency:

  1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations, gotchas, and common pitfalls
  2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility notes, and unsupported features
  3. Check if the library has specific CSS, rendering, or serialization constraints
  4. Check the library's weekly downloads and last publish date (is it maintained?)

  Output a structured report:
  ## Dependency Audit: [package-name]
  ### Known Limitations
  ### Gotchas for Our Use Case
  ### Risk Level (low/medium/high)
  ### Recommendation

  Be thorough ŌĆö silent failures from library limitations are the hardest bugs to catch in code review.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Include the dependency audit findings in the context given to ALL reviewers.

### Gate B: Functional Verification Evidence

Check the PR description for a **Verification** section. The dev agent is required to include:

- **For all PRs**: Build passes (`pnpm build` output or confirmation)
- **For UI/visual features**: Screenshot of the feature rendering in the browser
- **For features that produce output** (image export, PDF, file download): The actual output artifact or proof it's non-empty (file size, screenshot of result)
- **For API changes**: curl output showing the endpoint returns the expected response shape

If the PR description lacks verification evidence:
- **If part of /start-feature**: Message the dev agent via SendMessage: "PR is missing verification evidence. Add a Verification section to the PR description with [specific evidence needed]. See the pre-PR verification protocol."
- **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR needs verification evidence before review can proceed.

**Do NOT proceed to Step 3 until verification evidence is present.**

### Gate C: Visual Output Check (Conditional)

If the PR produces visual output (images, PDFs, charts, OG cards, share cards, exports):
- The exported/generated artifact MUST be attached to or linked from the PR description
- A reviewer must be able to visually inspect the output without running the code
- If missing, send PR back with: "This PR produces visual output ŌĆö attach the generated artifact to the PR description."

---

## Step 3: Run Parallel Independent Reviews (Round N)

**CRITICAL**: All reviews run in parallel. No reviewer sees another's comments. This prevents bias.

Track the current round number. Round 1 is the initial review. Round 2+ are follow-up reviews after fixes.

**For Round 1**: Launch all applicable reviewers (TA Insider, Domain Specialist(s), LLM Expert if applicable).
**For Round 2+**: Launch only targeted reviewers ŌĆö those whose prior findings had FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items that were addressed. Skip reviewers whose prior findings were all resolved or NOT APPLICABLE.

### Launch TA Insider Review (Always)

```
Task {
  name: "ta-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing a Phase 1 INSIDER review of PR #247 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 247
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 247

  Follow your Phase 1 review protocol:
  1. Read the PR description and any linked GitHub Issue
  2. Check if the change touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema)
  3. Review code against existing patterns in the codebase
  4. Check existing CLAUDE.md conventions compliance
  5. Verify data contract patterns are followed (if data flow changed)
  6. Check shadcn/ui and component conventions (if UI changes)

  ADDITIONAL CHECKS:
  7. If new dependencies were added, review the dependency audit findings: [INSERT DEP AUDIT IF APPLICABLE]
  8. If the PR produces visual output, verify the attached artifact looks correct
  9. Check that verification evidence in the PR description is credible (not just 'it works')

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## TA Review (Phase 1 - Insider): [PR Title] ŌĆö Round [N]
  ### Architecture Alignment
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: ­¤ö┤ FIX NOW, ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION, ­¤öĄ NOTE)
  ### Phase 1 Verdict

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

### Launch Domain Specialist Reviews (1-2, Dynamic)

For each selected specialist from Step 2, launch a review agent using the prompt template from `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md`. Use the `superpowers:code-reviewer` subagent type for all domain specialists.

**Important:** Copy the full prompt template from the specialist registry, including:
- The domain-specific checks (80% focus)
- The general engineering checks (20% focus)
- The **Runtime Verification Rule** (shared instruction ŌĆö include verbatim)
- The Round 2+ fix verification instructions (if applicable)

```
Task {
  name: "[domain]-specialist",          // e.g., "sql-specialist", "react-specialist"
  subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer",
  prompt: "[FULL PROMPT FROM docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md FOR THE SELECTED DOMAIN]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

**Example:** If Step 2 selected SQL/Database (primary) and React/Frontend (secondary), launch:

```
Task { name: "sql-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[SQL/Database prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
Task { name: "react-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[React/Frontend prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
```

### Launch LLM Expert Review (If Applicable ŌĆö Unchanged)

```
Task {
  name: "llm-expert-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "llm-expert",
  prompt: "You are performing an independent LLM EXPERT review of PR #247 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 247
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 247

  Review all LLM-related code for:
  - Prompt quality: clarity, specificity, output format constraints
  - Token efficiency: redundant instructions, over-prompting, prompt stuffing
  - Output consistency: structured output schemas, JSON mode, enum enforcement
  - Model selection: is the chosen model appropriate for the task complexity?
  - Resilience: handling malformed LLM output, timeouts, retries, rate limits
  - Cross-model compatibility: prompts that only work with one model family
  - Cost implications: token budget estimates, unnecessary Opus/GPT-4 usage for simple tasks
  - Streaming patterns: SSE implementation, partial response handling

  Rate each prompt on: clarity (1-5), token efficiency (1-5), output consistency (1-5), resilience (1-5).

  RUNTIME VERIFICATION RULE:
  When you encounter code where the runtime behavior is NOT self-evident from
  reading ŌĆö flag it as ­¤¤Ā VERIFY AT RUNTIME instead of reasoning about correctness.
  1. State what you THINK the behavior is
  2. State what the RISK is if you're wrong
  3. Require the dev to paste actual runtime output proving correctness

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## LLM Expert Review: [PR Title] ŌĆö Round [N]
  ### Prompt Quality Assessment
  ### Token Efficiency
  ### Model Selection
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: ­¤ö┤ FIX NOW, ­¤¤Ā VERIFY AT RUNTIME, ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION, ­¤öĄ NOTE)
  ### Recommendations

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Wait for ALL reviews to complete before proceeding.

---

## Step 4: TA Synthesis

After all reviews are collected, launch the TA synthesis pass:

```
Task {
  name: "ta-synthesizer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing Phase 2 SYNTHESIS for PR #247. This is review ROUND [N].

  The orchestrator will provide you with the independent review outputs (outsider, wild card if applicable, and LLM expert if applicable).

  Follow your Phase 2 synthesis protocol:
  1. Read all review comments (outsider, wild card, LLM expert)
  2. Re-review the PR with all reviews in context
  3. For each outsider/wild card/LLM expert comment, evaluate:
     - Does this conflict with project patterns or conventions?
     - Is this a valid point that should be applied?
     - Did you miss this in Phase 1?
  4. For each comment: AGREE or PUSHBACK WITH REASON
  5. Create the consolidated final list

  Output in the structured format:
  ## TA Synthesis (Phase 2): [PR Title] ŌĆö Round [N]
  ### Review of Outsider Comments
  ### Second Pass Findings
  ### Consolidated Review (For Dev Agent)
  - ­¤ö┤ FIX NOW items (MUST be resolved before merge)
  - ŌØī NOT APPLICABLE items with technical rationale
  - ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ ESCALATE TO FOUNDER items with reason
  - ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTIONS (non-blocking, dev's discretion)
  ### Final Verdict: [PASS ŌĆö ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED ŌĆö Round [N+1] needed]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

---

## Step 5: Deliver Results & Loop Decision

After synthesis is complete, check the Final Verdict:

### If PASS (0 FIX NOW items):

1. **Post final review summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **If part of /start-feature**: Message the PM agent that review is complete and PR is ready for founder merge.
3. **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR is approved.

### If CHANGES REQUIRED (1+ FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items):

1. **Post round summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **Send actionable items to dev agent** (or user if standalone):
   - List each FIX NOW item with clear description of what needs to change
   - List each VERIFY AT RUNTIME item with the specific runtime output needed
   - Reference specific files and line numbers where possible
3. **Wait for fixes to be pushed** ŌĆö dev agent pushes fix commits to the PR branch
4. **Post-fix re-verification gate (MANDATORY):**
   - Dev MUST re-run ALL functional verification commands from the original PR body
   - Dev MUST paste updated verification output as a PR comment
   - If the PR had curl examples, re-run them and paste the responses
   - If the PR had screenshot evidence, re-capture after fixes
   - For VERIFY AT RUNTIME items, dev MUST paste the specific runtime output requested
   - **Fixes without re-verification evidence are not considered complete**
5. **Go back to Step 3** with Round N+1, targeting only the reviewers whose areas were affected

### Loop Safety

- **Max 4 rounds** ŌĆö if FIX NOW items remain after 4 rounds, ESCALATE TO FOUNDER with full context
- **Round 2+ is targeted** ŌĆö only re-invoke reviewers whose prior FIX NOW items were addressed (don't re-run all 4 reviewers for a one-line fix)
- **New issues found during fix verification count as new FIX NOW items** ŌĆö the loop continues

### PR Comment Template

```bash
gh pr comment 247 --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Triple-Layer Code Review ŌĆö Round [N] of [TOTAL]

### Reviewers
| Role | Domain | This Round |
|------|--------|------------|
| TA (Insider) | Architecture, types, schema | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 1 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 2 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |
| LLM Expert | Prompt quality, token efficiency | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |

### Pre-Review Gates
- [ ] New dependency audit: [PASS/N/A]
- [ ] Functional verification evidence: [PASS ŌĆö describe what was verified]
- [ ] Visual output attached: [PASS/N/A]

### Issues Found & Resolution
#### ­¤ö┤ FIX NOW
[List from synthesis ŌĆö empty if PASS]

#### ­¤¤Ā VERIFY AT RUNTIME
[Items requiring runtime evidence ŌĆö empty if none]

#### ŌØī NOT APPLICABLE
[List with technical rationale]

#### ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTIONS
[Non-blocking items]

### Post-Fix Verification
[For Round 2+: paste re-run of original functional verification commands + VERIFY AT RUNTIME evidence]

**Round [N] verdict: [PASS ŌĆö Ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED ŌĆö see FIX NOW / VERIFY AT RUNTIME items]**
EOF
)"
```

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Reviews MUST be independent** ŌĆö no reviewer sees another's output during Phase 1
- **TA synthesis is authoritative** ŌĆö TA can mark specialist comments as "NOT APPLICABLE" with technical justification, EXCEPT for VERIFY AT RUNTIME items (see below)
- **VERIFY AT RUNTIME items cannot be dismissed** ŌĆö TA synthesis MUST NOT mark these as NOT APPLICABLE. They require runtime evidence from the dev before they can be resolved
- **Domain specialists are selected dynamically** ŌĆö see Step 2 and `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the registry
- **Always post summary to GitHub PR** ŌĆö this creates the audit trail
- **Review loops until 0 FIX NOW and 0 VERIFY AT RUNTIME items** ŌĆö a single pass is not sufficient if blocking issues exist
- **Post-fix re-verification is mandatory** ŌĆö after Round N fixes, dev must re-run ALL functional verification from the PR body and paste updated output
- **Pre-review gates are mandatory** ŌĆö missing verification evidence blocks the review from starting
- **Max 4 rounds** ŌĆö escalate to founder if review doesn't converge
- **Round 2+ is targeted** ŌĆö don't waste reviewer cycles re-reviewing areas with no changes

<teammate-message teammate_id="cli-specialist" color="purple" summary="Node/CLI Specialist review for PR #247">
## Node/CLI Specialist Review: feat(cli): insights command ŌĆö Round 1

### Async Safety

**No issues found.** All async operations are properly awaited:
- `runner.runAnalysis()` awaited in both passes (lines 867, 912 in diff)
- `syncSingleFile()` awaited before analysis proceeds (line 988)
- `readStdin()` returns a proper Promise, awaited in `insightsCommand` (line 971)
- No fire-and-forget patterns, no unhandled rejection risk
- DB operations via `better-sqlite3` are synchronous (correct ŌĆö no async needed)

### File System & I/O

**stdin handling is solid.** The `readStdin()` function (lines 1058-1070):
- Correctly checks `process.stdin.isTTY` to avoid hanging when no pipe is connected ŌĆö resolves with `'{}'` which will fail JSON parse gracefully later (since `session_id` will be missing)
- Sets encoding to `utf-8` before reading (correct)
- Listens for `'error'` event and rejects the promise (correct)
- Concatenates chunks and trims on `'end'` (standard pattern)

**`syncSingleFile`** (lines 1085-1095): Takes a `filePath` string and passes it directly to `provider.parse()`. No path manipulation needed since the caller (Claude Code hook) provides the absolute path. Acceptable.

### CLI UX & Design

- **Exit codes**: `process.exit(1)` on error in both `insightsCommand` and `insightsCheckCommand` (correct)
- **Quiet mode**: Consistently respects `--quiet` flag ŌĆö suppresses all `console.log` output, only writes machine-readable count in `insights check -q`
- **Error messages**: Prefixed with `[Code Insights]` and colored via chalk (matches existing CLI conventions)
- **Commander registration** (lines 1226-1245): Clean subcommand structure. `insights [session_id]` with optional positional arg + `insights check` subcommand

### Issues Found

**­¤ö┤ FIX NOW ŌĆö Migration function ordering violates project convention**

In `cli/src/db/migrate.ts`, `applyV8()` is defined BEFORE `applyV7()` in the file (diff lines 1153-1158). The project convention documented in MEMORY states: "Migration functions must be in chronological order in migrate.ts (applyV2, applyV3, applyV4, applyV5)." While JavaScript hoists function declarations so this works at runtime, it breaks the established convention and will confuse future maintainers scanning the file.

**Fix:** Move `applyV8()` definition after `applyV7()`.

---

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `deleteSessionInsights` uses dynamic SQL construction**

The `deleteSessionInsights` function (lines 552-570) builds SQL with dynamic `WHERE` clauses and spreads params via `...params`. While this is safe because all values go through parameterized `?` placeholders (no SQL injection risk), the `db.prepare(...).run(...params)` spread pattern is unusual for this codebase.

Consider: This works correctly with `better-sqlite3` since `.run()` accepts variadic params. No action required, just flagging the non-standard spread pattern.

---

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `estimated_cost_usd` is always 0**

Both `saveAnalysisUsage` calls (lines 889-901, 929-941) pass `estimated_cost_usd: 0`. This is presumably intentional for the initial implementation (cost estimation may come later), but worth confirming this is deliberate rather than a missed calculation.

---

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `insightsCheckCommand` is synchronous but could benefit from error boundary consistency**

`insightsCheckCommand` (lines 1015-1054) is a synchronous function that calls `getDb()` and runs queries. If `getDb()` throws (e.g., DB not initialized), the `try/catch` handles it. However, the function signature is `void` (not `Promise<void>`) ŌĆö this is correct since there's no async work, just noting it's consistent.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö No timeout on stdin read**

The `readStdin()` function has no timeout. If a pipe is connected but never closes (e.g., a hung parent process), the CLI will hang indefinitely. In hook mode, Claude Code is the caller and will always close stdin, so this is acceptable for the current use case. If this function is ever reused outside hook mode, a timeout should be added.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö `buildCacheableConversationBlock` returns `ContentBlock` but only `.text` is used**

Lines 865 and 910 access `.text` from the `ContentBlock` returned by `buildCacheableConversationBlock()`. This discards the `cache_control` metadata. This is correct for the CLI path ŌĆö cache control is only meaningful when sending to the Anthropic API via the provider, and the runner abstraction handles prompt construction internally. The CLI just needs the formatted text.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö Inline DB helpers duplicate server logic**

The PR body explains this: "DB writes are inline (no circular `@code-insights/server` import)." The comment at line 507 also documents this. Functions like `saveInsightsToDb`, `saveFacetsToDb`, `deleteSessionInsights`, and `saveAnalysisUsage` mirror `server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts`. This is an acceptable trade-off to avoid circular cross-package imports in a monorepo, but creates a maintenance burden ŌĆö changes to the insights schema must be updated in two places.

### Verdict

**APPROVE with one required fix.** The code is well-structured, async-safe, and follows established CLI patterns. The stdin handling is robust, the resume detection logic is clean, and the two-pass analysis flow is clear.

**Required before merge:**
1. Move `applyV8()` function definition after `applyV7()` in `migrate.ts` to maintain chronological ordering convention.

**Optional improvements (non-blocking):**
- Confirm `estimated_cost_usd: 0` is intentionally deferred
- Consider extracting shared DB helpers to a `cli/src/db/analysis.ts` module in a future PR to reduce duplication with server
</teammate-message>

### Data Contract Impact

### Pattern Consistency

- [x] Command registration matches existing pattern (Commander `.command()` + `.action()` in `index.ts`)
- [x] SQLite queries use prepared statements throughout
- [x] `INSERT OR REPLACE` used for upsert (matches server-side `analysis-db.ts` and `analysis-usage-db.ts` patterns)
- [x] Transaction wrapping for batch insight inserts (line 539-549 of diff)

- [x] PQ category normalization at write time matches server-side `convertPromptQualityToInsightRow` behavior
- [x] Runner interface used correctly (`ClaudeNativeRunner.validate()` + `new ClaudeNativeRunner()` for native, `ProviderRunner.fromConfig()` for provider)

### Architecture Alignment

The decision to inline DB helpers rather than import from `@code-insights/server` is architecturally sound ŌĆö it avoids a circular dependency (CLI -> server -> CLI). The inline helpers mirror the server-side functions in `analysis-db.ts` and `analysis-usage-db.ts` closely enough that behavior will be consistent. The comment at line 473 ("mirror server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts, no cross-package import") documents the rationale.

### Issues Found

**FIX NOW:**

1. **`applyV8()` function defined out of chronological order** ŌĆö In `migrate.ts`, `applyV8()` is placed BEFORE `applyV7()` in the source file (line 153 vs line 159 of the diff). Project convention (documented in MEMORY.md) requires migration functions in chronological order. The *call site* in `runMigrations()` is correct (V7 before V8), but the function definition order should match. Move `applyV8()` AFTER `applyV7()`.

2. **Server-side `saveAnalysisUsage()` will clobber `session_message_count` on re-analysis via dashboard** ŌĆö The server's `analysis-usage-db.ts:47` uses `INSERT OR REPLACE` with only 11 columns (no `session_message_count`). If a user re-analyzes a session from the dashboard (server path), the `INSERT OR REPLACE` will delete the existing row (including `session_message_count`) and insert a new one with NULL for that column. This breaks resume detection for any session previously analyzed via CLI.

   **Fix:** Update `server/src/llm/analysis-usage-db.ts` to include `session_message_count` in its INSERT statement (pass NULL when called from server ŌĆö the server doesn't know message count, but at least it won't clobber an existing value). Alternatively, change the server's upsert to use `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT ... DO UPDATE` which only overwrites specified columns.

   **Note:** This is technically a server-side change not in this PR's scope, but the data contract is broken if both paths write to the same table. The CLI writes `session_message_count`, the server overwrites it with NULL. This must be addressed either in this PR or as a tracked follow-up with the server fix merged before or alongside this PR.

**SUGGESTIONS:**

3. **`estimated_cost_usd: 0` hardcoded for both analysis passes** ŌĆö Lines 898 and 938 always write `0` for cost. The server-side analysis path computes actual cost via `calculateCost()` in `analysis-pricing.ts`. For native mode (`claude -p`) this is correct (no API cost), but for provider mode the cost should be computed. This means CLI-initiated provider analysis will show $0.00 cost in the dashboard, unlike server-initiated analysis. Consider importing and calling the pricing calculator, or document this as a known limitation.

4. **Missing `[pattern-monitor]` console.warn** ŌĆö The server's `saveFacetsToDb` (line 281) emits `[pattern-monitor] saveFacetsToDb: effective_pattern missing category field` when a pattern lacks a category. The CLI's inline version silently falls back to `'uncategorized'` without the warning. For monitoring parity, add the same console.warn.

**NOTES:**

5. **`buildCacheableConversationBlock()` returns a `ContentBlock` but `.text` is accessed** ŌĆö Line 865: `buildCacheableConversationBlock(formattedMessages).text`. The function returns `{ type: 'text', text: string, cache_control?: ... }`, so `.text` is correct. But note that the cache_control marker is lost since only the text is extracted. This means the CLI path does not benefit from Anthropic prompt caching even in provider mode. This is likely intentional (the runner handles prompt construction differently), but worth confirming.

6. **`readStdin()` returns `'{}'` when stdin is a TTY** ŌĆö Line 1063. This means `--hook` with no piped input silently parses `{}`, which then fails on the `session_id` check. This is fine ŌĆö the error path is clear. Just noting the design choice.

### Phase 1 Verdict

**Changes Required** ŌĆö Two items need resolution before merge:

1. **FIX NOW #1** (function ordering) ŌĆö trivial fix, 30 seconds
2. **FIX NOW #2** (server-side `session_message_count` clobber) ŌĆö requires either a server-side fix in this PR or a tracked companion PR. The data contract is broken without it: dashboard re-analysis will silently break CLI resume detection. At minimum, the dev should confirm with the founder whether this ships as a companion fix or blocks this PR.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="sql-specialist" color="orange" summary="SQL/Database Specialist Review PR #247 Round 1">
## SQL/Database Specialist Review: feat(cli): insights command ŌĆö Round 1

### SQL Correctness

All queries use **parameterized statements** (`db.prepare(...).run(?, ?, ...)`) ŌĆö no string interpolation of user-supplied values into SQL. This is correct and safe.

**Dynamic query construction in `deleteSessionInsights`** (insights.ts lines ~117-135): The `DELETE FROM insights WHERE ${conditions.join(' AND ')}` pattern builds the WHERE clause dynamically, but the dynamic parts are only column names and `NOT IN (?, ?, ...)` placeholders ŌĆö never user input. The actual values flow through `params` array. This matches the identical pattern in `server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts:240-261`. **Safe.**

**INSERT OR REPLACE semantics**: Used for `insights`, `session_facets`, and `analysis_usage` ŌĆö all have defined primary keys. `INSERT OR REPLACE` will delete the existing row and insert a new one, which resets any columns not explicitly set (e.g., `analyzed_at` on `analysis_usage` gets re-defaulted to `datetime('now')`). This is the intended upsert behavior here. **Correct.**

### Query Performance

1. **`loadSessionMessages`** ŌĆö `SELECT ... FROM messages WHERE session_id = ? ORDER BY timestamp ASC`. The `messages` table should have an index on `session_id`. Verified: the base schema (V1) creates `messages` with a `session_id` column that's used as a foreign key. No explicit index seen in the diff, but this is an existing pattern used elsewhere.

2. **`insightsCheckCommand`** ŌĆö The LEFT JOIN query to find unanalyzed sessions:
   ```sql
   SELECT s.id FROM sessions s
   LEFT JOIN analysis_usage au ON au.session_id = s.id AND au.analysis_type = 'session'
   WHERE s.started_at >= ? AND s.deleted_at IS NULL AND au.analysis_type IS NULL
   ```
   This is a standard anti-join pattern. The `analysis_usage` table has PK `(session_id, analysis_type)` which covers the join. `sessions.started_at` may benefit from an index for large databases, but for a local tool this is fine. **No issue.**

3. **`isAlreadyAnalyzed`** ŌĆö Single-row lookup on `analysis_usage` by `(session_id, analysis_type)` ŌĆö covered by the primary key. **Optimal.**

### Migration Review

**applyV8 function ordering** (migrate.ts):

­¤ö┤ **FIX NOW ŌĆö `applyV8` is defined BEFORE `applyV7` in the file.**

In the diff, the new `applyV8` function is inserted at line 153 (after `applyV6`), while `applyV7` remains at line 158. The project convention (documented in MEMORY.md) states: *"Migration functions must be in chronological order in migrate.ts (applyV2, applyV3, applyV4, applyV5)"*. The `applyV8` function body appears before `applyV7` in the file:

```
function applyV6(db) { ... }   // line ~129

function applyV8(db) { ... }   // line ~153  ŌåÉ OUT OF ORDER

function applyV7(db) { ... }   // line ~158
```

The execution order in `runMigrations()` is correct (V7 runs before V8), so this is a **file organization issue only** ŌĆö it does not affect runtime behavior. But it violates the project convention and will confuse future readers.

**Fix:** Move `applyV8` to after `applyV7` in the file.

---

**Migration idempotency**: `applyV8` uses `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` which will throw if the column already exists. However, the `currentVersion < 8` guard prevents re-execution. Combined with `INSERT OR IGNORE INTO schema_version`, this follows the established pattern (same as V5, V6). **Correct.**

**V8 migration content**: `ALTER TABLE analysis_usage ADD COLUMN session_message_count INTEGER` ŌĆö nullable INTEGER column, no default. Existing rows get NULL. **Correct and backward compatible.**

### Issues Found

**­¤ö┤ FIX NOW**

1. **Migration function ordering** ŌĆö `applyV8` is defined before `applyV7` in the source file. Must be reordered to maintain chronological convention. (No runtime impact, but violates project convention.)

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION**

2. **Test seed helper uses string interpolation in SQL** (insights.test.ts lines ~74-82):
   ```typescript
   function seedSession(db, id = 'sess1', messageCount = 10): void {
     db.exec(`
       INSERT OR IGNORE INTO sessions
         (...) VALUES ('${id}', 'p1', ...${messageCount});
     `);
   }
   ```
   This uses template literal interpolation (`'${id}'`, `${messageCount}`) directly in SQL. Since this is a **test-only** helper with hardcoded caller values (never user input), it's not a security risk. However, it doesn't match the parameterized pattern used everywhere else. Consider using `db.prepare(...).run(...)` for consistency. **Low priority ŌĆö test code only.**

3. **Inline DB helpers duplicate server code** ŌĆö `saveInsightsToDb`, `deleteSessionInsights`, `saveFacetsToDb`, `convertToInsightRows`, `convertPQToInsightRow` in `insights.ts` are near-identical copies of `server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts`. The PR description explains this is intentional ("CLI cannot import from @code-insights/server"), and the `saveFacetsToDb` inline version drops the `console.warn` monitor. The duplication is a conscious trade-off. **Acknowledged ŌĆö no action needed now**, but consider extracting shared DB helpers to the CLI package long-term.

4. **`saveFacetsToDb` inline version uses hardcoded `ANALYSIS_VERSION`** ŌĆö The server version accepts `analysisVersion` as a parameter (`saveFacetsToDb(sessionId, facets, analysisVersion)`), while the CLI inline version hardcodes it via the module-level `ANALYSIS_VERSION` constant. Both currently resolve to `'3.0.0'`. This is fine since the CLI controls its own analysis version, but note the divergence from the server API.

5. **`deleteSessionInsights` inline version is missing `includeOnlyTypes`** ŌĆö The server version in `analysis-db.ts:250-253` supports an `includeOnlyTypes` option. The CLI inline copy omits it. This is fine since the CLI code never uses that option, but note it if the CLI later needs it.

**­¤öĄ NOTE**

6. **`INSERT OR REPLACE` on `analysis_usage` resets `analyzed_at`** ŌĆö Because SQLite's `INSERT OR REPLACE` deletes the existing row first, the `analyzed_at` column (which defaults to `datetime('now')`) gets reset on re-analysis. This is correct behavior (you want the timestamp of the latest analysis), just noting it's intentional.

7. **Resume detection compares `session_message_count` with strict equality** (`===`) ŌĆö If `session_message_count` in the DB is NULL (pre-V8 rows or rows written by the server's V7 `saveAnalysisUsage` which doesn't include this column), `NULL === number` is `false` in JS, so `isAlreadyAnalyzed` returns `false` ŌĆö meaning the session gets re-analyzed. This is the correct and safe behavior for the upgrade path.

8. **No transaction wrapping the full analysis write** ŌĆö The two-pass analysis (session + PQ) writes insights, facets, and usage in separate statements. If the process crashes between Pass 1 and Pass 2, you'll have session insights but no PQ insights. This is acceptable for a CLI tool (re-run with `--force` to fix), and the `deleteSessionInsights` + `saveInsightsToDb` pairs within each pass are individually consistent.

### Verdict

**APPROVE with one required fix.**

The SQL patterns are clean and safe. All queries use parameterized statements, the migration is idempotent, and the resume detection logic handles edge cases (NULL comparisons, upgrade path) correctly.

**Required before merge:**
- Move `applyV8` function definition after `applyV7` in `migrate.ts` to maintain chronological ordering convention.

Everything else is solid.
</teammate-message>

# /start-feature ŌĆö Auto-Setup Feature Development Team

**Feature**: refactor: move analysis DB helpers from server to CLI (Option A deduplication)

You are setting up a hybrid agent team for feature development. The PM agent leads the team and owns the ceremony. Your job is minimal setup, then hand control to PM.

---

## Step 1: Create Git Worktree

Slugify the feature description into a branch name:
- Take `refactor: move analysis DB helpers from server to CLI (Option A deduplication)`, lowercase it, replace spaces/special chars with hyphens, truncate to 50 chars
- Prefix with `feature/` (e.g., "add demo mode onboarding" -> `feature/add-demo-mode-onboarding`)

```bash
# Example (adapt the slug from refactor: move analysis DB helpers from server to CLI (Option A deduplication)):
BRANCH_NAME="feature/<slugified-arguments>"
git fetch origin
git worktree add ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} -b ${BRANCH_NAME} origin/main
```

If the worktree or branch already exists, inform the user and ask how to proceed.

Run `pnpm install` in the worktree:
```bash
cd ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} && pnpm install
```

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root ŌĆö must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ ŌĆö must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server ŌĆö do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary
[What this PR does]

## Dependency Audit (if NEW_DEPS)
[Library name]: [Known limitations found, or 'No significant limitations found']

## Verification
- Build: PASS
- Tests: PASS
- [Screenshot of feature rendering] (if VISUAL)
- [Screenshot/proof of output artifact] (if OUTPUT_ARTIFACT)
- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

## During Review Rounds

If the review team sends back FIX NOW items:
1. Read each item carefully
2. Implement the fixes in the worktree
3. Re-run applicable verification tiers (at minimum Tier 1)
4. If fixes are visual, re-capture screenshots
5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable ŌĆö thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

## Step 5: Supervise

After spawning agents, your role is active supervisor:

1. **PM handles scoping and task graph** ŌĆö orchestrator handles all agent spawning
2. **Spawn agents when PM sends SPAWN_REQUEST messages**
3. **Intervene when**:
   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user
   - An agent is stuck or reports a blocker -> help unblock
   - PM sends a REVIEW_REQUEST -> run `/start-review` on the PR number
4. **Review loop management**:
   - `/start-review` handles the loop internally (runs rounds until 0 FIX NOW items)
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, relay them to the dev-agent via SendMessage
   - After dev pushes fixes, `/start-review` re-runs targeted reviewers automatically
   - If review hits max rounds (4) without converging, escalate to user
5. **When PM reports "ready for merge"** -> inform the user

## Step 6: Cleanup (After PR Merge)

After the founder merges the PR:

1. Send shutdown requests to all teammates (pm-agent, ta-agent, dev-agent)
2. Delete the team: `TeamDelete`
3. Clean up worktree:
```bash
git worktree remove ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>
```
4. Confirm cleanup is complete

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** ŌĆö sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** ŌĆö it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** ŌĆö spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** ŌĆö agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes ŌĆö PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** ŌĆö build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** ŌĆö orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** ŌĆö dev agent must kill any server it starts

<teammate-message teammate_id="sql-specialist" color="orange" summary="SQL/DB specialist review for PR #249">
## SQL/Database Specialist Review: Move analysis DB helpers from server to CLI ŌĆö Round 1

### SQL Correctness

All SQL statements use parameterized queries throughout. No string interpolation of user-supplied values. The dynamic WHERE construction in `deleteSessionInsights` builds placeholders with `.map(() => '?')` and passes values via `params` array ŌĆö safe pattern, column names are hardcoded.

**`saveInsightsToDb`**: Uses `INSERT OR REPLACE` with 16 columns, wrapped in `db.transaction()`. Correct ŌĆö identical to both the old server and old CLI inline versions.

**`saveFacetsToDb`**: Uses `INSERT OR REPLACE INTO session_facets` with 9 columns. Query text is identical to the server original. The `analysisVersion` parameter now has a default value (`= ANALYSIS_VERSION`), which is a clean convergence ŌĆö server callers passed it explicitly, CLI inline used the constant directly.

**`deleteSessionInsights`**: Gains `includeOnlyTypes` option from the server version. The `type IN (...)` clause uses parameterized placeholders. Safe and correct.

**`getSessionAnalysisUsage`**: SELECT query with 12 columns, `ORDER BY analyzed_at ASC`. Identical to the server original.

### Query Preservation

Queries are preserved with the following intentional convergences:

1. **Defensive `?? []` guards** on `response.decisions`, `response.learnings`, `response.findings`, `response.takeaways` ŌĆö added from the CLI inline version. These protect against malformed LLM output where typed fields might be undefined at runtime. Safe, strictly more defensive.

2. **`workflow_pattern ?? null`** in `saveFacetsToDb` ŌĆö the CLI version adds this guard; the server original passed the raw value. In better-sqlite3, `undefined` maps to `null` anyway, so this is functionally identical but more explicit.

3. **`course_correction_reason`** ŌĆö the old CLI inline had `?? null`, the server original didn't. The new version drops the guard (matches server). Functionally equivalent per better-sqlite3 binding semantics.

4. **`alternatives` filter** ŌĆö server used `a && typeof a === 'object' && a.option`, CLI uses `Boolean(a?.option)` with a type guard. Functionally equivalent.

### Issues Found

**­¤ö┤ FIX NOW: `saveAnalysisUsage` will clobber `session_message_count` on server re-analysis**

The old server `saveAnalysisUsage` intentionally **excluded** `session_message_count` from both the INSERT column list and the ON CONFLICT SET clause. The comment even documented this: *"preserves columns not in this write (e.g. session_message_count written by the CLI insights command)"*.

The new unified version in `cli/src/analysis/analysis-usage-db.ts` includes `session_message_count` in **both** INSERT and ON CONFLICT SET. When server callers invoke this (via re-export) without providing `session_message_count`, the `?? null` fallback writes `NULL`, **overwriting** a previously CLI-written value.

**Impact**: After a server-side re-analysis (backfill, dashboard "re-analyze" button), the `session_message_count` for that session will be set to NULL. The next CLI hook run will fail to detect the session as "already analyzed" (resume detection), causing unnecessary re-analysis.

**Fix**: Either:
- (A) Change the ON CONFLICT SET to conditionally preserve: `session_message_count = COALESCE(excluded.session_message_count, analysis_usage.session_message_count)` ŌĆö this writes the new value when provided, preserves the old value when NULL.
- (B) Omit `session_message_count` from the ON CONFLICT SET clause entirely when the value is null (requires two prepared statements or dynamic SQL).

Option (A) is cleanest ŌĆö single statement, correct semantics.

---

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION: `convertPQToInsightRow` naming alias**

The server originally exported `convertPromptQualityToInsightRow`. The CLI names it `convertPQToInsightRow` and the re-export adds `convertPQToInsightRow as convertPromptQualityToInsightRow`. This works, but the canonical name is now the abbreviated form. If future server code imports the short name, readability drops slightly. Low priority ŌĆö the alias handles backward compat correctly.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE: `[pattern-monitor]` console.warn preserved**

The `saveFacetsToDb` in the CLI version preserves the `[pattern-monitor]` console.warn for missing category fields. This is correct ŌĆö the monitor was present in the server version and is documented in MEMORY.md as intentional.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE: `sessionData` adapter in insights.ts**

The `sessionData` adapter at line ~130 of the diff converts `SessionRow` (null-based, from SQLite) to `SessionData` (undefined-based, shared type) via `?? undefined`. This is correct ŌĆö `null` from SQLite rows should become `undefined` for the optional fields on `SessionData`. The three fields handled (`compact_count`, `auto_compact_count`, `slash_commands`) match the optional fields on the interface.

---

**­¤öĄ NOTE: Transaction safety preserved**

`saveInsightsToDb` still wraps batch inserts in `db.transaction()`. Single-row operations (`saveFacetsToDb`, `saveAnalysisUsage`, `deleteSessionInsights`) don't need explicit transactions (single statement = implicit transaction in SQLite). Correct.

### Verdict

**Request changes** ŌĆö one fix required before merge.

The `session_message_count` clobber in `saveAnalysisUsage` (­¤ö┤) is a real behavioral regression that breaks the resume-detection contract between CLI and server. The fix is a one-line change to use `COALESCE(excluded.session_message_count, analysis_usage.session_message_count)` in the ON CONFLICT SET clause.

All other SQL is correct, parameterized, and faithfully preserves the original queries with safe defensive convergences.
</teammate-message>

### Module Resolution & Exports

**ESM imports: PASS.** All new CLI files use `.js` extensions in relative imports (`../db/client.js`, `./prompt-types.js`, `./pattern-normalize.js`, `./prompt-quality-normalize.js`). No CommonJS `require()` anywhere.

| Server consumer | Imports | Re-exported? |
|---|---|---|
| `analysis.ts` | `ANALYSIS_VERSION`, `convertToInsightRows`, `saveInsightsToDb`, `deleteSessionInsights`, `saveFacetsToDb`, `type InsightRow`, `type SessionData` | All present |

| `route-helpers.ts` | `type SessionData` | Present |
| `analysis-usage-db.ts` consumers | `saveAnalysisUsage`, `getSessionAnalysisUsage`, types | All present |

The `convertPQToInsightRow as convertPromptQualityToInsightRow` alias correctly preserves the server's longer function name.

### Import Cleanup

**Dead imports removed from `insights.ts`: PASS.**
- `randomUUID` from `crypto` ŌĆö removed (now in `analysis-db.ts`)
- `normalizePatternCategory` ŌĆö removed
- `normalizePromptQualityCategory` ŌĆö removed
- `ANALYSIS_VERSION` constant ŌĆö removed (now imported transitively via the DB helpers)
- `PromptQualityResponse` type import ŌĆö removed (no longer needed inline)
- Inline `InsightRow` interface ŌĆö removed (now imported from `analysis-db.ts`)
- ~170 lines of inline DB helper functions ŌĆö removed

**No dead imports remain.** The new imports (`saveInsightsToDb`, `deleteSessionInsights`, `saveFacetsToDb`, `convertToInsightRows`, `convertPQToInsightRow`, `saveAnalysisUsage`) are all actively used in the remaining code.

### Issues Found

**No ­¤ö┤ FIX NOW issues.**

---

­¤¤Ī **SUGGESTION: `sessionData` adapter ŌĆö `null` to `undefined` conversion is partial**

In `insights.ts`, the adapter converts `compact_count`, `auto_compact_count`, and `slash_commands` from `null` (SQLite) to `undefined` (SessionData). However, `SessionData.summary` is typed as `string | null`, while `SessionRow.summary` is also `string | null` ŌĆö so that field passes through correctly. The spread `...session` also carries `message_count` from `SessionRow`, which is not on `SessionData` ŌĆö this is harmless due to TypeScript structural typing but worth noting for documentation clarity.

No action needed ŌĆö this is correct as-is.

---

­¤¤Ī **SUGGESTION: `saveFacetsToDb` default parameter divergence is intentional but worth a comment**

The old server version had `analysisVersion: string` (required, no default). The new CLI version has `analysisVersion: string = ANALYSIS_VERSION` (optional with default). Server callers pass `ANALYSIS_VERSION` explicitly, so behavior is unchanged. The CLI caller relies on the default. This is a correct convergence of the two copies, but the server re-export wrapper doesn't document this signature change. Since all server callers pass the value explicitly, there's no risk.

---

­¤¤Ī **SUGGESTION: `SaveAnalysisUsageData.analysis_type` union broadened**

The old server type was `'session' | 'prompt_quality'`. The new CLI type adds `'facet'`. This is correct ŌĆö `facet-extraction.ts` already passes `'facet'` at runtime (line 85), so the old server type was actually too narrow. Good fix.

---

­¤öĄ **NOTE: Defensive `?? []` guards on `decisions`/`learnings` are a behavior change from server version**

The old server `convertToInsightRows` iterated `response.decisions` and `response.learnings` directly (no nullish coalescing). The new CLI version uses `response.decisions ?? []` and `response.learnings ?? []`. This is safer against malformed LLM responses and matches what the old CLI inline code was doing. Both the CLI and server now share this defensive behavior ŌĆö a net improvement.

Similarly, `convertPQToInsightRow` now uses `(response.findings ?? [])` and `(response.takeaways ?? [])` where the old server version accessed them directly. Same improvement.

---

­¤öĄ **NOTE: `[pattern-monitor]` console.warn preserved**

The `saveFacetsToDb` function in the new CLI location preserves the `[pattern-monitor]` warning for missing category fields. This monitor was in the server version and is correctly carried over.

---

­¤öĄ **NOTE: `chunk_count` parameterization**

The old CLI inline `saveAnalysisUsage` hardcoded `chunk_count` to `1` in the SQL. The new version parameterizes it as `data.chunk_count ?? 1`. This is correct ŌĆö the CLI always passes 1 (non-chunked), and the server can now benefit from the same function for chunked analysis.

### Verdict

**APPROVE.** This is a clean, well-executed deduplication. The module resolution is correct, all re-exports are complete, ESM conventions are followed, no circular dependencies exist, and the behavioral convergences (defensive `?? []` guards, `analysis_type` union broadening, `chunk_count` parameterization) are all improvements. The `sessionData` adapter in `insights.ts` correctly bridges the `null`/`undefined` gap between SQLite rows and the shared `SessionData` type. TDD tests cover the key logic paths. No blocking issues found.

# /start-feature ŌĆö Auto-Setup Feature Development Team

**Feature**: feat: update install-hook to add SessionEnd analysis hook (GitHub Issue #241)

You are setting up a hybrid agent team for feature development. The PM agent leads the team and owns the ceremony. Your job is minimal setup, then hand control to PM.

---

## Step 1: Create Git Worktree

Slugify the feature description into a branch name:
- Take `feat: update install-hook to add SessionEnd analysis hook (GitHub Issue #241)`, lowercase it, replace spaces/special chars with hyphens, truncate to 50 chars
- Prefix with `feature/` (e.g., "add demo mode onboarding" -> `feature/add-demo-mode-onboarding`)

```bash
# Example (adapt the slug from feat: update install-hook to add SessionEnd analysis hook (GitHub Issue #241)):
BRANCH_NAME="feature/<slugified-arguments>"
git fetch origin
git worktree add ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} -b ${BRANCH_NAME} origin/main
```

If the worktree or branch already exists, inform the user and ask how to proceed.

Run `pnpm install` in the worktree:
```bash
cd ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} && pnpm install
```

---

## Step 2: Create Named Team

Create the team using TeamCreate. Use the slugified branch name (without `feature/` prefix) as the team name:

```
TeamCreate {
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  description: "Feature team: feat: update install-hook to add SessionEnd analysis hook (GitHub Issue #241)"
}
```

---

```
Task {
  name: "pm-agent",

   - Task: 'TA: Review architecture alignment' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if internal-only (new components, UI, styling)

   - Task: 'Dev: Implement feature in worktree' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Dev: Verify feature and create PR' (blockedBy: above) -- includes pre-PR verification protocol
   - Task: 'Review: Triple-layer code review (loops until 0 FIX NOW)' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Post final review summary to GitHub PR' (blockedBy: above)

   IMPORTANT ŌĆö Classify the feature scope for Dev's verification protocol:

   - Does it add new npm dependencies? ŌåÆ Tag: NEW_DEPS
   - Does it change API endpoints? ŌåÆ Tag: API_CHANGE
   Include these tags in the GitHub Issue so Dev knows which verification tiers apply.

5. REQUEST AGENT SPAWNS: When your handoff task is done, message the orchestrator:
   - If TA is needed: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: ta-agent ŌĆö [brief context]'
   - When dev prerequisites are met: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: dev-agent ŌĆö [brief context including issue number and key details]'
   The orchestrator will spawn the agents and assign tasks.

   SKIP TA if the feature is internal-only (new components, UI fixes, styling, LLM provider additions). In that case, mark the TA task as completed with note 'Skipped -- internal-only change'.

   If the feature involves LLM calls (prompts, model selection, token budgets, structured output):
   - 'SPAWN_REQUEST: llm-expert-agent ŌĆö [brief context about the LLM aspect]'
   The LLM Expert will design the prompt architecture, token budget, and model recommendation before dev implements.

   SKIP LLM Expert if the feature doesn't touch LLM code. Mark the task as completed with note 'Skipped -- no LLM impact'.

6. MONITOR: Check TaskList periodically.
   - When Dev creates a PR, message the orchestrator: 'REVIEW_REQUEST: PR #XX is ready for /start-review'
   - The orchestrator will run /start-review which loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, the orchestrator sends them to Dev. Dev fixes and pushes. Review re-runs automatically.
   - You do NOT need to request additional review rounds ŌĆö the loop is built into /start-review.

7. REPORT: When review converges (0 FIX NOW items) and final summary is posted, message the orchestrator: 'PR #XX for feat: update install-hook to add SessionEnd analysis hook (GitHub Issue #241) is ready for founder review and merge.'

IMPORTANT RULES:
- NEVER merge PRs -- founder-only
- NEVER try to spawn agents -- message the orchestrator instead

- If you need user clarification, message the orchestrator who will ask the user
- You can message existing teammates directly via SendMessage for routine coordination
- Task dependencies enforce ceremony order -- don't skip steps

  mode: "bypassPermissions"

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root ŌĆö must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ ŌĆö must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server ŌĆö do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary

- Tests: PASS

- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable ŌĆö thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** ŌĆö sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** ŌĆö it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** ŌĆö spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** ŌĆö agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes ŌĆö PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** ŌĆö build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** ŌĆö orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** ŌĆö dev agent must kill any server it starts
