<teammate-message teammate_id="cli-specialist" color="purple" summary="Node/CLI Specialist Review for PR #250 ŌĆö Round 1">
## Node/CLI Specialist Review: Update install-hook for SessionEnd analysis hook ŌĆö Round 1

### File System Safety

**Settings.json read/write is reasonably safe.** The existing pattern ŌĆö `existsSync` check, `readFileSync` + `JSON.parse` in a try/catch with fallback to empty object, `mkdirSync({ recursive: true })` before write ŌĆö is adequate for a single-user CLI tool. No race conditions are realistically possible since only the user runs this command manually.

**Non-atomic write:** `fs.writeFileSync` is not atomic (no write-to-temp + rename pattern). If the process crashes mid-write, `settings.json` could be corrupted. However, the file is small (typically <1KB) and this matches the existing pattern that was already in production. Not a regression.

**Malformed JSON handling:** Covered ŌĆö the existing try/catch around `JSON.parse` logs a warning and falls back to `{}`. This means a corrupted settings.json won't crash, but will silently discard existing settings. This is pre-existing behavior, not introduced by this PR.

### CLI UX & Flags

**Flag registration is correct.** In `cli/src/index.ts`, `--sync-only` and `--analysis-only` are registered via `.option()` and Commander.js will camelCase them to `syncOnly` and `analysisOnly`. The action handler maps them explicitly: `installHookCommand({ syncOnly: opts.syncOnly, analysisOnly: opts.analysisOnly })`.

**Output messaging is clear.** The default case explains both hooks with their purposes. The `--sync-only` and `--analysis-only` cases show targeted messages. The "already installed" messages are per-hook-type, which is good UX.

**"How it works" section after install** conditionally shows relevant info based on which hooks were installed. Good.

### Issues Found

**­¤ö┤ FIX NOW ŌĆö No mutual exclusion for `--sync-only` + `--analysis-only`**

If a user passes both `--sync-only` and `--analysis-only`, the logic resolves to:
```
installSync = !analysisOnly = false
installAnalysis = !syncOnly = false
```
Neither hook gets installed. The function hits the `!syncInstalled && !analysisInstalled` guard and prints "Code Insights hooks already installed" with a suggestion to uninstall first ŌĆö which is misleading because nothing was installed.

This is a logic bug. Options:
1. Add a check at the top: if both flags are set, print an error and return.
2. Treat both flags as equivalent to default (install both).

Option 1 is cleaner ŌĆö these flags are intentionally mutually exclusive.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `process.argv[1]` for CLI path**

The hook command is constructed as `node ${cliPath} sync -q` where `cliPath = process.argv[1]`. This is pre-existing behavior (not introduced by this PR), but worth noting:

- When installed via `npm link`, `argv[1]` is the symlinked path (e.g., `/usr/local/lib/node_modules/@code-insights/cli/dist/index.js`) ŌĆö works fine.
- When run via `npx`, `argv[1]` points to a cache path that may change between runs ŌĆö the hook could break after cache cleanup.
- When installed globally via `npm install -g`, `argv[1]` is stable ŌĆö works fine.

This is a pre-existing concern, not a regression. But the new `SessionEnd` hook amplifies the blast radius since a broken path now affects two hooks instead of one.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö Missing `SessionEnd` in `ClaudeSettings` interface (in diff, not in Read)**

The diff adds `SessionEnd?: HookConfig[];` to the `ClaudeSettings` interface ŌĆö good. But the Read tool showed the old file without it. Confirming from the diff that this is included. Correct.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö Duplicate detection uses `includes('code-insights')`**

The `hookAlreadyInstalled` helper checks if any hook command string `.includes('code-insights')`. This is a reasonable heuristic but would false-positive on a hypothetical third-party tool whose command path happens to contain "code-insights". Low risk in practice ŌĆö the user's `~/.claude/settings.json` is unlikely to have such a collision.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö Test safety concern: tests operate on real `~/.claude/settings.json`**

The tests back up and restore `~/.claude/settings.json` via `beforeEach`/`afterEach`. This is functional but risky:
- If a test crashes before `afterEach` runs, the real settings file could be corrupted or deleted.
- The `tmpDir` created in `beforeEach` is never actually used ŌĆö the tests still read/write `HOOKS_FILE` which points to the real `~/.claude/settings.json`.

The backup/restore pattern mitigates this, and `vi.resetModules()` ensures fresh imports. But a more robust approach would be to mock `os.homedir()` to point to `tmpDir`. This is a pre-existing pattern concern if other test files do the same thing.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö `uninstallHookCommand` does not track telemetry**

The `installHookCommand` tracks `cli_install_hook` events, but `uninstallHookCommand` has no telemetry tracking. This is pre-existing ŌĆö the PR didn't change the uninstall function's telemetry behavior. Worth noting for future work.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö ESM compliance is clean**

All imports use `.js` extensions (`../utils/telemetry.js`). No CommonJS `require()`. The test file imports via `await import('../install-hook.js')` after `vi.resetModules()` ŌĆö correct pattern for module re-isolation in Vitest.

### Verdict

**Request changes.** One logic bug needs fixing:

The `--sync-only` + `--analysis-only` mutual exclusion gap (­¤ö┤) will silently do nothing and print a misleading message. This is a straightforward fix ŌĆö add a guard at the top of `installHookCommand`. Everything else is solid: the hook structure matches Claude Code's settings schema, duplicate detection works per-hook-type, cleanup on uninstall properly handles empty arrays/objects, and test coverage is comprehensive (15 tests covering install/uninstall/duplicate/preservation/cleanup scenarios).

</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="cli-reviewer-r2" color="pink" summary="Node/CLI Specialist Review PR #250 Round 2">
## Node/CLI Specialist Review: PR #250 ŌĆö Round 2

### Fix Verification

The Round 1 issue (`--sync-only` + `--analysis-only` mutual exclusion) has been **correctly fixed**.

1. **Guard placement**: Lines 47-50 in the diff ŌĆö the guard is the FIRST logic after destructuring options, before any file I/O or settings reads. Correct placement.
2. **Error message**: `chalk.red('Cannot use --sync-only and --analysis-only together. Use neither flag to install both hooks.')` ŌĆö clear, actionable, tells the user what to do instead.
3. **Guard condition**: `syncOnly && analysisOnly` ŌĆö both are boolean flags defaulting to `false`, so no falsy-value edge cases. Commander.js passes `true` when the flag is present, `undefined` when absent, and the destructuring default `= false` handles that.
4. **Test exists**: The `--sync-only + --analysis-only mutual exclusion` describe block verifies that when both flags are set, no hooks file is written (`expect(fs.existsSync(HOOKS_FILE)).toBe(false)`). This is a solid assertion ŌĆö it proves neither hook was installed.

**Verdict on fix: PASS**

---

### Fresh Pass Findings

#### Complete Flag Flow Analysis

| Scenario | Stop hook | SessionEnd hook | Behavior |
|---|---|---|---|
| Default `{}` | Installed | Installed | `installSync=true`, `installAnalysis=true` |
| `--sync-only` | Installed | Skipped | `installSync=true`, `installAnalysis=false` |
| `--analysis-only` | Skipped | Installed | `installSync=false`, `installAnalysis=true` |
| Both flags | Neither | Neither | Early return with error |

The boolean logic `installSync = !analysisOnly` and `installAnalysis = !syncOnly` correctly implements this matrix. All four paths are tested.

#### Uninstall Path

The uninstall function correctly:
- Filters both `Stop` and `SessionEnd` arrays independently
- Deletes empty arrays (`if (settings.hooks.Stop.length === 0) delete settings.hooks.Stop`)
- Cleans up empty `hooks` object
- Tests cover: both hooks removed, non-code-insights hooks preserved (Stop and SessionEnd separately), missing settings.json, empty hooks cleanup

#### SessionEnd Hook Command

The command string is: `node ${cliPath} insights --hook --native -q` with `timeout: 120000`. This matches the PR description and the `insights` command's expected flags. The 120s timeout is reasonable for a 15-30s analysis operation.

---

### Issues Found

#### ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION: Mutual exclusion test could also verify error output

The test at line 148 only checks that no hooks file was written. It does not verify that the error message was actually printed. Consider adding a `console.log` spy to assert the chalk.red message was called. This would prevent a regression where someone removes the error message but keeps the early return.

```ts
const consoleSpy = vi.spyOn(console, 'log');
await installHookCommand({ syncOnly: true, analysisOnly: true });
expect(consoleSpy).toHaveBeenCalledWith(expect.stringContaining('Cannot use'));
```

Not blocking ŌĆö the current test is sufficient for correctness.

#### ­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION: `ClaudeSettings` interface is missing `SessionEnd` in the diff

Looking at the diff, `SessionEnd` was added to the interface:
```ts
hooks?: {
    PostToolUse?: HookConfig[];
    Stop?: HookConfig[];
    SessionEnd?: HookConfig[];  // added
    [key: string]: HookConfig[] | undefined;
};
```

This is fine, but the `PostToolUse` entry was already there from before and is never used in this file. Not an issue introduced by this PR ŌĆö just noting it.

#### ­¤öĄ NOTE: Tests read/write real `~/.claude/settings.json`

The tests back up and restore the real `settings.json` file in beforeEach/afterEach. This is a pragmatic approach since the code under test hardcodes the path. However, if a test crashes mid-run (e.g., OOM kill, SIGKILL), the backup won't be restored. The tmpDir created in beforeEach is unused ŌĆö it was likely intended for isolation but the approach pivoted to backup/restore.

This is an existing risk pattern, not introduced by this PR, and the backup/restore logic is correct for normal test runs.

#### ­¤öĄ NOTE: `analysisCommand` variable computed but unused when `syncOnly: true`

When `syncOnly` is true, `analysisCommand` is still computed on line ~68 of the new code. This is trivially cheap (string interpolation) and not worth optimizing ŌĆö just noting for completeness.

---

### Verdict

**APPROVE** ŌĆö The mutual exclusion fix is correctly implemented and tested. The flag flow matrix is complete and correct. The uninstall path handles both hook types properly. No blocking issues found.

The two suggestions (console spy in mutual exclusion test, unused tmpDir cleanup) are minor improvements that can be addressed in a follow-up if desired.
</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="ta-reviewer-r2" color="cyan" summary="TA Phase 1 Insider Review PR #250 Round 2">
## TA Review (Phase 1 - Insider): PR #250 ŌĆö Round 2

### Fix Verification

**Round 1 Issue: `--sync-only` + `--analysis-only` mutual exclusion bug**

The fix (commit `5b673c6`) is correctly implemented:

```typescript
if (syncOnly && analysisOnly) {
  console.log(chalk.red('Cannot use --sync-only and --analysis-only together. Use neither flag to install both hooks.'));
  return;
}
```

- Guard is placed at the **top of the function**, before the `try` block ŌĆö correct placement, no side effects before early return.
- Clear error message tells the user what to do instead.
- Returns early without writing any files ŌĆö confirmed by test (`expect(fs.existsSync(HOOKS_FILE)).toBe(false)`).
- No new issues introduced by this commit.

**Verdict: Fix is correct and complete.**

### Architecture Alignment

**1. `ClaudeSettings` interface includes `SessionEnd`?**
Yes. Line 14 of the PR branch adds `SessionEnd?: HookConfig[]` to the `ClaudeSettings.hooks` type. The index signature `[key: string]: HookConfig[] | undefined` also provides forward-compat for other event types, which is good.

**2. Server re-exports?**
N/A ŌĆö no server changes in this PR. Correct, this is CLI-only.

**3. `settings.json` write path safe?**
Yes. The pattern is:
- `fs.mkdirSync(CLAUDE_SETTINGS_DIR, { recursive: true })` ŌĆö creates `~/.claude/` if missing
- `fs.writeFileSync(HOOKS_FILE, JSON.stringify(settings, null, 2))` ŌĆö atomic write with pretty-print
- Existing settings are loaded first and merged, not overwritten (test confirms `theme: 'dark'` preserved)

**4. Uninstall handles both hook types?**
Yes. The uninstall function:
- Checks `!settings.hooks?.Stop && !settings.hooks?.SessionEnd` for early exit
- Filters both `Stop` and `SessionEnd` arrays independently
- Deletes empty arrays, deletes empty `hooks` object
- Preserves non-code-insights hooks in both arrays (confirmed by tests)

**5. Telemetry tracking for install?**
Yes. `trackEvent('cli_install_hook', { success, hook_types, sync_installed, analysis_installed })` ŌĆö includes which hook types were installed. Good for analytics.

**6. Hook command strings correct?**
- **Stop**: `node ${cliPath} sync -q` ŌĆö Correct. Matches existing behavior.
- **SessionEnd**: `node ${cliPath} insights --hook --native -q` with `timeout: 120000` ŌĆö Correct. Matches the `insights` command flags defined in `index.ts` (lines 125-128: `--native`, `--hook`, `-q`).

**7. `InstallHookOptions` is internal only?**
Yes. Exported as `export interface InstallHookOptions` from `install-hook.ts`, consumed only by `index.ts` via Commander option mapping. No types.ts impact, no schema impact. Correct.

**8. Commander wiring in `index.ts`?**
```typescript
.option('--sync-only', 'Install only the Stop (sync) hook')
.option('--analysis-only', 'Install only the SessionEnd (analysis) hook')
.action((opts) => installHookCommand({ syncOnly: opts.syncOnly, analysisOnly: opts.analysisOnly }))
```
Commander auto-camelCases `--sync-only` ŌåÆ `opts.syncOnly` and `--analysis-only` ŌåÆ `opts.analysisOnly`. Mapping is correct.

**9. Duplicate detection?**
The extracted `hookAlreadyInstalled()` helper is clean. It checks per-hook-type independently, so having a Stop hook doesn't block installing a SessionEnd hook. Tests confirm idempotency for both types.

**10. Test quality?**
- 334 lines, 15 tests covering: default install, sync-only, analysis-only, mutual exclusion, duplicate detection, uninstall (both types, preservation, empty cleanup, missing file).
- Tests write to the **real** `~/.claude/settings.json` path with backup/restore in beforeEach/afterEach. This is a pragmatic choice given `HOOKS_FILE` is a module-level constant. The backup/restore pattern is solid.

### Issues Found

No issues found. The Round 1 FIX NOW item has been correctly addressed. The implementation is clean, the architecture is aligned, and the test coverage is thorough.

# /start-feature ŌĆö Auto-Setup Feature Development Team

**Feature**: feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242)

You are setting up a hybrid agent team for feature development. The PM agent leads the team and owns the ceremony. Your job is minimal setup, then hand control to PM.

---

## Step 1: Create Git Worktree

Slugify the feature description into a branch name:
- Take `feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242)`, lowercase it, replace spaces/special chars with hyphens, truncate to 50 chars
- Prefix with `feature/` (e.g., "add demo mode onboarding" -> `feature/add-demo-mode-onboarding`)

```bash
# Example (adapt the slug from feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242)):
BRANCH_NAME="feature/<slugified-arguments>"
git fetch origin
git worktree add ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} -b ${BRANCH_NAME} origin/main
```

If the worktree or branch already exists, inform the user and ask how to proceed.

Run `pnpm install` in the worktree:
```bash
cd ../code-insights-${BRANCH_NAME#feature/} && pnpm install
```

---

## Step 2: Create Named Team

Create the team using TeamCreate. Use the slugified branch name (without `feature/` prefix) as the team name:

```
TeamCreate {
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  description: "Feature team: feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242)"
}
```

---

## Step 3: Spawn PM Agent

The PM agent handles scoping, GitHub Issues, and task graph creation. It does NOT spawn other agents ŌĆö only the orchestrator can spawn agents.

```
Task {
  name: "pm-agent",
  subagent_type: "product-manager",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the PM for this feature team.

FEATURE REQUEST: feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242)
WORKTREE: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/
BRANCH: feature/<slugified-arguments>
TEAM: feat-<slugified-arguments>

Your responsibilities are scoping, GitHub Issues, task graph, and handoff preparation.
IMPORTANT: You CANNOT spawn agents. Only the orchestrator can. When you need an agent spawned, message the orchestrator with the request.

Follow this protocol:

1. SCOPE: Read docs in docs/ and CLAUDE.md to understand what this feature involves. Check for existing design docs in docs/plans/. Check docs/architecture/ for architecture context. If the scope is unclear, message the orchestrator for clarification.

2. ISSUES: Search for an existing GitHub Issue that matches this feature. If one exists, use it. If not, create one with proper description, acceptance criteria, and T-shirt size. Record the issue number.

3. TASK GRAPH: Create the ceremony tasks using TaskCreate, then set dependencies with TaskUpdate:
   - Task: 'TA: Review architecture alignment' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if internal-only (new components, UI, styling)
   - Task: 'LLM Expert: Design prompt architecture' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if feature doesn't involve LLM calls
   - Task: 'PM: Prepare handoff context in GitHub Issue' (no dependencies, you do this yourself)
   - Task: 'Dev: Read handoff and design docs, prepare questions' (blockedBy: TA + LLM Expert if applicable + PM handoff)
   - Task: 'Dev + TA: Reach consensus on implementation approach' (blockedBy: above) -- SKIP if internal-only
   - Task: 'Dev: Implement feature in worktree' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Dev: Verify feature and create PR' (blockedBy: above) -- includes pre-PR verification protocol
   - Task: 'Review: Triple-layer code review (loops until 0 FIX NOW)' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Post final review summary to GitHub PR' (blockedBy: above)

4. DO YOUR OWN TASK: Work on your handoff task -- prepare context in the GitHub Issue (description, acceptance criteria, relevant doc paths, implementation guidance).

   IMPORTANT ŌĆö Classify the feature scope for Dev's verification protocol:
   - Does it touch UI/visual rendering? ŌåÆ Tag: VISUAL
   - Does it produce output artifacts (images, PDFs, exports)? ŌåÆ Tag: OUTPUT_ARTIFACT
   - Does it add new npm dependencies? ŌåÆ Tag: NEW_DEPS
   - Does it change API endpoints? ŌåÆ Tag: API_CHANGE
   Include these tags in the GitHub Issue so Dev knows which verification tiers apply.

5. REQUEST AGENT SPAWNS: When your handoff task is done, message the orchestrator:
   - If TA is needed: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: ta-agent ŌĆö [brief context]'
   - When dev prerequisites are met: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: dev-agent ŌĆö [brief context including issue number and key details]'
   The orchestrator will spawn the agents and assign tasks.

   SKIP TA if the feature is internal-only (new components, UI fixes, styling, LLM provider additions). In that case, mark the TA task as completed with note 'Skipped -- internal-only change'.

   If the feature involves LLM calls (prompts, model selection, token budgets, structured output):
   - 'SPAWN_REQUEST: llm-expert-agent ŌĆö [brief context about the LLM aspect]'
   The LLM Expert will design the prompt architecture, token budget, and model recommendation before dev implements.

   SKIP LLM Expert if the feature doesn't touch LLM code. Mark the task as completed with note 'Skipped -- no LLM impact'.

6. MONITOR: Check TaskList periodically.
   - When Dev creates a PR, message the orchestrator: 'REVIEW_REQUEST: PR #XX is ready for /start-review'
   - The orchestrator will run /start-review which loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, the orchestrator sends them to Dev. Dev fixes and pushes. Review re-runs automatically.
   - You do NOT need to request additional review rounds ŌĆö the loop is built into /start-review.

7. REPORT: When review converges (0 FIX NOW items) and final summary is posted, message the orchestrator: 'PR #XX for feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242) is ready for founder review and merge.'

IMPORTANT RULES:
- NEVER merge PRs -- founder-only
- NEVER try to spawn agents -- message the orchestrator instead
- All dev work happens in the worktree
- If you need user clarification, message the orchestrator who will ask the user
- You can message existing teammates directly via SendMessage for routine coordination
- Task dependencies enforce ceremony order -- don't skip steps
- PRE-PR GATE (MANDATORY): Before any PR is created, Dev must complete the full verification protocol (see Dev agent instructions). GitHub Actions costs money ŌĆö failed CI runs are wasted spend.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Task {

  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the TA task to ta-agent.

**For LLM Expert (if PM requests it):**
```
Task {
  name: "llm-expert-agent",
  subagent_type: "llm-expert",

  prompt: "You are the LLM Expert for feature team feat-<slugified-arguments>. Feature: feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242). Check TaskList for your assigned tasks. Design the prompt architecture, token budget, model recommendation, and output schema for the LLM aspects of this feature. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent and ta-agent. Mark tasks in_progress when starting, completed when done.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the LLM Expert task to llm-expert-agent.

**For Dev (when PM requests it):**
```
Task {
  name: "dev-agent",
  subagent_type: "engineer",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the Dev for feature team feat-<slugified-arguments>. Feature: feat: backfill check + recovery for unanalyzed sessions (GitHub Issue #242). Worktree: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/. All code work happens in the worktree. Check TaskList for your tasks. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent. Mark tasks in_progress/completed.

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root ŌĆö must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ ŌĆö must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server ŌĆö do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary
[What this PR does]

## Dependency Audit (if NEW_DEPS)
[Library name]: [Known limitations found, or 'No significant limitations found']

## Verification
- Build: PASS
- Tests: PASS
- [Screenshot of feature rendering] (if VISUAL)
- [Screenshot/proof of output artifact] (if OUTPUT_ARTIFACT)
- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

## During Review Rounds

If the review team sends back FIX NOW items:
1. Read each item carefully
2. Implement the fixes in the worktree
3. Re-run applicable verification tiers (at minimum Tier 1)
4. If fixes are visual, re-capture screenshots
5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable ŌĆö thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

---

## Step 5: Supervise

After spawning agents, your role is active supervisor:

1. **PM handles scoping and task graph** ŌĆö orchestrator handles all agent spawning
2. **Spawn agents when PM sends SPAWN_REQUEST messages**
3. **Intervene when**:
   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user
   - An agent is stuck or reports a blocker -> help unblock
   - PM sends a REVIEW_REQUEST -> run `/start-review` on the PR number
4. **Review loop management**:
   - `/start-review` handles the loop internally (runs rounds until 0 FIX NOW items)
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, relay them to the dev-agent via SendMessage
   - After dev pushes fixes, `/start-review` re-runs targeted reviewers automatically
   - If review hits max rounds (4) without converging, escalate to user
5. **When PM reports "ready for merge"** -> inform the user

---

## Step 6: Cleanup (After PR Merge)

After the founder merges the PR:

1. Send shutdown requests to all teammates (pm-agent, ta-agent, dev-agent)
2. Delete the team: `TeamDelete`
3. Clean up worktree:
```bash
git worktree remove ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>
```
4. Confirm cleanup is complete

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** ŌĆö sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** ŌĆö it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** ŌĆö spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** ŌĆö agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes ŌĆö PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** ŌĆö build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** ŌĆö orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** ŌĆö dev agent must kill any server it starts

<teammate-message teammate_id="cli-specialist" color="purple" summary="Node/CLI Specialist Review for PR #252">
## Node/CLI Specialist Review: insights check -- count-based behavior + --analyze flag ŌĆö Round 1

### Async Safety & Error Resilience

**Async wiring is correct.** The `insightsCheckCommand` function signature changed from sync `void` to `async Promise<void>`, and the Commander action in `index.ts` properly `await`s it. No unhandled promise rejections possible from the wiring layer.

**Batch error resilience is solid.** The `--analyze` loop catches per-session errors, logs them via `console.error`, and continues processing. The `successCount` tracks only successful analyses, so the summary line accurately reflects results. The auto-analyze path (1-2 sessions) also has a `catch` block that silently swallows errors ŌĆö appropriate for the "opportunistic background analysis" UX.

**Runner reuse pattern is correct.** `ClaudeNativeRunner.validate()` is called once before the loop, and the runner instance is passed via `_runner` to `runInsightsCommand`, which correctly skips re-construction and re-validation when `_runner` is present. This avoids N `execFileSync('claude', ['--version'])` calls.

### CLI UX

**Count-based dispatch thresholds are well-designed:**
- 0: silent exit (correct for hook usage)
- 1-2: auto-analyze silently (zero friction for small backlogs)
- 3-10: count + suggestion (no time estimate ŌĆö appropriate)
- 11+: count + time estimate + suggestion (sets expectations)

**Progress format** `[N/total] title ... done (Xs)` is clear and standard. Failed sessions print `failed` followed by a red error line on stderr ŌĆö good separation of progress (stdout) from errors (stderr).

**`--quiet` correctly outputs just the number** via `process.stdout.write` (no chalk, no prefix) ŌĆö suitable for scripting (`count=$(code-insights insights check -q)`).

### Issues Found

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö SQL query change: `au.analysis_type IS NULL` to `au.session_id IS NULL`**
(`cli/src/commands/insights.ts`, diff line in the SELECT query)

The old query used `AND au.analysis_type IS NULL` to detect unjoined rows. The PR changes this to `AND au.session_id IS NULL`. Both are semantically correct for a LEFT JOIN (any non-nullable column from the right table works), but `session_id IS NULL` is slightly more idiomatic for "no matching row found." This is a neutral change ŌĆö not a bug, just noting the diff includes it.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `_runner` as a public interface field is a mild code smell**
(`cli/src/commands/insights.ts:100`)

The `_runner` field on `InsightsCommandOptions` is prefixed with `_` to signal "internal," but it's on a public exported interface. This works fine today since it's only used by `insightsCheckCommand` calling `runInsightsCommand` internally. If the interface grows or becomes part of a public API contract, consider a separate internal overload or options type. Low priority ŌĆö acceptable for now.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö Auto-analyze (1-2 sessions) silently swallows all errors**
(`cli/src/commands/insights.ts`, the `count <= 2` block)

The empty `catch {}` means if `validate()` succeeds but every analysis fails (e.g., claude CLI hangs or crashes), the user gets zero feedback. For 1-2 sessions this is likely fine (the intent is "opportunistic"), but consider at minimum a `--verbose` path in the future. Not blocking.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö `SECONDS_PER_SESSION = 22` constant**
The 22-second estimate is reasonable for native runner (spawns `claude -p` subprocess per call). If provider-runner (direct API) is ever supported for `--analyze`, the estimate would be too high. The constant is clearly scoped to the current implementation, so this is fine.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö Sequential processing is intentional and correct**
`--analyze` processes sessions one at a time in a `for` loop. This is the right call for `claude -p` which spawns a subprocess ŌĆö parallelizing would risk resource exhaustion and interleaved output. No change needed.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö Test coverage is thorough**
13 new tests covering all 4 count tiers, `--days` window, `--analyze` progress output, error resilience, and edge case (0 sessions with `--analyze`). The `seedSessions` helper with `analyzedCount` parameter is clean. Tests correctly use `process.stdout.write` spy for progress lines and `console.log` spy for summary lines, matching the implementation's output channels.

### Verdict

**APPROVE.** Clean implementation with correct async patterns, good error resilience, well-designed UX thresholds, and thorough test coverage. The three suggestions above are all low-priority and non-blocking. No bugs, no async hazards, no CLI UX issues found.
</teammate-message>

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user is implementing Phase 12 ("Native Analysis via Claude Code Hooks") of the Code Insights project (v4.8.0). This phase enables zero-config session analysis by leveraging Claude Code's `SessionEnd` hook and `claude -p` non-interactive mode. The user requested implementation of GitHub Issues #240, #248, #241, and #242 with full development ceremony (`/start-feature`), TDD, and triple-layer code reviews with multiple Claude expert personas. Each feature was implemented via isolated git worktrees, PM-led scoping, dev agent implementation, and multi-reviewer code review loops. The user explicitly required all reviewer suggestions (not just FIX NOW items) to be addressed before merge.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **SQLite `INSERT OR REPLACE` vs `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`**: `INSERT OR REPLACE` deletes the entire row then inserts, clobbering unspecified columns. `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` is a true upsert that preserves unspecified columns. Critical for shared writers.
   - **`COALESCE(excluded.col, table.col)`**: SQLite pattern for "use new value if provided, keep existing if NULL." Used in `saveAnalysisUsage` to protect `session_message_count` from server-side clobber.
   - **AnalysisRunner interface**: `ClaudeNativeRunner` (execFileSync ŌåÆ `claude -p`) and `ProviderRunner` (wraps existing LLM client). Stateless, safe to reuse.
   - **Resume detection**: `session_message_count` in `analysis_usage` (V8 migration). If count unchanged since last analysis, skip. If changed (session resumed), re-analyze.
   - **Claude Code Hooks API**: Events are top-level keys in `~/.claude/settings.json` under `hooks`. Valid events: `PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, `Stop`, `SubagentStop`, `SessionStart`, `SessionEnd`, `UserPromptSubmit`, `PreCompact`, `Notification`. All hooks receive stdin JSON: `{ session_id, transcript_path, cwd, permission_mode, hook_event_name }`.
   - **`import.meta.url` for stable CLI path**: Replaces `process.argv[1]` which is unstable under `npx`. `fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)` resolves relative to the package.
   - **Test isolation via `os.homedir()` mock**: Mock `os.homedir()` to temp dir + `vi.resetModules()` + dynamic import so module-level constants pick up the mock. Eliminates risk of corrupting real `~/.claude/settings.json`.
   - **`/start-feature` ceremony**: worktree ŌåÆ TeamCreate ŌåÆ PM agent (scopes, creates issue, task graph, handoff) ŌåÆ Dev agent (TDD implementation) ŌåÆ Triple-layer review (TA Insider + Domain Specialist + TA Synthesis) ŌåÆ Founder merge ŌåÆ cleanup.
   - **Monorepo dependency direction**: `server ŌåÆ imports from ŌåÆ @code-insights/cli`. CLI cannot import from server (circular). Solution: move shared code to CLI, server re-exports.

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`cli/src/commands/insights.ts`** (Created in PR #247, modified in #249, #252)
     - Core `insights` CLI command with `--native`, `--hook`, `--force`, `--quiet`, `--source` flags
     - `insightsCommand()`: orchestrates runner selection, two-pass analysis (session + PQ), DB writes
     - `insightsCheckCommand()`: finds unanalyzed sessions, count-based dispatch (0/1-2/3-10/11+), `--analyze` batch processing
     - `readStdin()`: reads JSON from stdin for hook mode, returns `'{}'` for TTY
     - `syncSingleFile()`: targeted single-session sync without full provider scan
     - In PR #249: ~170 lines of inline DB helpers replaced with imports from `../analysis/analysis-db.js` and `../analysis/analysis-usage-db.js`
     - `sessionData` adapter bridges `null` (SQLite) ŌåÆ `undefined` (SessionData interface)

   - **`cli/src/analysis/analysis-usage-db.ts`** (Created in PR #249, critical COALESCE fix)
     - Moved from `server/src/llm/analysis-usage-db.ts`
     - `saveAnalysisUsage()` with `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` and `COALESCE` for `session_message_count`
     - `SaveAnalysisUsageData` interface with optional `session_message_count?: number`
     - `getSessionAnalysisUsage()` for table cohesion
     - Key SQL: `session_message_count = COALESCE(excluded.session_message_count, analysis_usage.session_message_count)`

   - **`cli/src/analysis/analysis-db.ts`** (Created in PR #249)
     - Moved from `server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts`
     - `saveInsightsToDb()`, `deleteSessionInsights()` (with `includeOnlyTypes`), `saveFacetsToDb()` (with `analysisVersion` parameter + default), `convertToInsightRows()`, `convertPQToInsightRow()`
     - `ANALYSIS_VERSION` exported as constant, accepted as parameter with default
     - Preserves `[pattern-monitor]` and `[pq-monitor]` console.warn monitors
     - Defensive `?? []` guards on `decisions`, `learnings`, `findings`, `takeaways`

   - **`cli/src/commands/install-hook.ts`** (Modified in PR #250)
     - `installHookCommand(options: InstallHookOptions)`: installs both `Stop` (sync) + `SessionEnd` (analysis) hooks
     - Mutual exclusion guard: `if (syncOnly && analysisOnly) { error + return }`
     - `CLI_ENTRY = path.resolve(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url), '../../index.js')` ŌĆö stable path
     - `uninstallHookCommand()`: filters both `Stop` and `SessionEnd` arrays, cleans empty objects
     - SessionEnd hook: `node ${CLI_ENTRY} insights --hook --native -q` with `timeout: 120000`

   - **`cli/src/commands/__tests__/install-hook.test.ts`** (Created in PR #250)
     - 15+ tests with `os.homedir()` mocked to temp dir via `vi.mock('os', ...)` factory
     - `_mockOs = { homeDir: '' }` mutable object pattern for ESM hoisting
     - Console spy verifies error messages printed
     - No backup/restore of real settings.json

   - **`cli/src/db/migrate.ts`** (Modified in PR #247)
     - `applyV8()`: `ALTER TABLE analysis_usage ADD COLUMN session_message_count INTEGER`
     - Functions in chronological order: applyV6 ŌåÆ applyV7 ŌåÆ applyV8
     - `CURRENT_SCHEMA_VERSION` bumped to 8 in `schema.ts`

   - **`server/src/llm/analysis-db.ts`** and **`server/src/llm/analysis-usage-db.ts`** (Rewritten as re-exports in PR #249)
     - Thin re-export wrappers from `@code-insights/cli/analysis/*`
     - `convertPQToInsightRow as convertPromptQualityToInsightRow` alias for backward compat

   - **`cli/package.json`** (Modified in PRs #249)
     - Added exports: `./analysis/analysis-db`, `./analysis/analysis-usage-db`

   - **`cli/src/index.ts`** (Modified in PRs #247, #250, #252)
     - Registered `insights` command + `insights check` subcommand
     - Added `--sync-only`, `--analysis-only` flags on `install-hook`
     - Added `--analyze`, `--days` flags on `insights check`

4. Errors and Fixes:

   - **Migration function ordering (PR #247)**: `applyV8()` was defined before `applyV7()` in migrate.ts. All 3 reviewers caught this. Fixed by moving the function definition after `applyV7()`. Project convention requires chronological order.

   - **Server-side `INSERT OR REPLACE` clobber (PR #247)**: The server's `saveAnalysisUsage()` used `INSERT OR REPLACE` with 11 columns (no `session_message_count`). This would DELETE the row (including CLI-written `session_message_count`) and INSERT a new one with NULL. Fixed by changing to `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`. User initially asked "why different columns?" which led to Option A discussion. User decided: Option C (ON CONFLICT) for this PR, Option A (move to CLI) immediately after.

   - **`session_message_count` COALESCE missing (PR #249)**: After moving `saveAnalysisUsage` to CLI as the canonical version, the unified function included `session_message_count` in the ON CONFLICT SET clause. When server callers pass NULL (they don't provide it), this overwrites CLI-written values. SQL specialist caught this. Fixed with `COALESCE(excluded.session_message_count, analysis_usage.session_message_count)`.

   - **`--sync-only` + `--analysis-only` mutual exclusion (PR #250)**: Both flags set = neither hook installed with misleading output. Both reviewers caught independently. Fixed with guard at top of function.

   - **Items 3 & 4 not implemented by dev (PR #250)**: Dev initially only addressed items 1-2 (console spy, consolidated message) but not items 3-4 (`process.argv[1]` replacement, test isolation). I verified via grep, caught the gap, and sent explicit instructions back. Dev then implemented all in one commit.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Circular dependency between CLI and server**: Solved by moving shared code to CLI package, server becomes re-exports. Follows PR #238 precedent.
   - **Shared upsert with different column subsets**: `COALESCE` pattern in ON CONFLICT SET preserves columns one writer cares about when the other doesn't provide them.
   - **Claude Code `SessionEnd` event verification**: Used Context7 MCP to query official docs. Confirmed `SessionEnd` is valid ŌĆö plan doc was correct.
   - **Stable CLI path for hooks**: `process.argv[1]` is unstable under npx. Replaced with `import.meta.url` resolution which is stable across npm link, global install, and npx.
   - **Test isolation**: Real `~/.claude/settings.json` was being modified by tests with fragile backup/restore. Fixed by mocking `os.homedir()` to temp dir.

<teammate-message teammate_id="react-specialist" color="purple" summary="React/Frontend Specialist Review PR #253 Round 1">
## React/Frontend Specialist Review: PR #253 ŌĆö Round 1

**PR:** feat: dashboard + docs updates for Phase 12 native analysis
**Files reviewed:** `LlmNudgeBanner.tsx`, `AnalysisCostLine.tsx`, `useAnalysisCost.ts`, `README.md`, `ROADMAP.md`
**Additions:** 97 | **Deletions:** 50

---

### Component Quality

**LlmNudgeBanner rewrite** ŌĆö Well-structured dual-path CTA. The refactor from a flat `COPY` record (with `title` + `description`) to `TITLES`-only is clean; the description text is now inline in JSX, which makes sense given the two paths have different copy. The dashed border box for the hook path creates a clear visual hierarchy: primary (hook) vs secondary (provider config). The `or` divider pattern (flex + border-t + uppercase label) is a standard UI pattern, properly implemented.

**AnalysisCostLine native branch** ŌĆö Follows the existing `allOllama` detection pattern exactly, which is the right call for consistency. The early return for `allNative` before the `allOllama`/legacy branching is correctly ordered ŌĆö native sessions should never fall through to cost display.

---

### Accessibility

The `LlmNudgeBanner` retains `role="status"` on the outer container and `aria-label="Dismiss"` on the close button ŌĆö good. The `<code>` element for the install command is semantically correct for a terminal command.

The new `AnalysisCostLine` native branch returns a static `<div>` without the Popover wrapper. This is correct ŌĆö there's no cost breakdown to show for native analysis, so no interactive element is needed. The `select-none` class is present on the wrapper, consistent with the non-popover path for legacy sessions.

No new interactive elements were introduced without keyboard support. The existing `<a>` for Ollama and `<Link>` for Settings remain keyboard-navigable.

---

### Performance

No performance concerns. No new hooks, no new queries, no new state. The `allNative` check is `Array.every()` on what is typically 1-3 rows ŌĆö negligible. The `totalDurationMs` reduce runs on the same small array. No unnecessary re-renders introduced.

---

### Issues Found

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `LlmNudgeBanner`: `Terminal` icon import is new but only used in the hook path**

The `Terminal` import from `lucide-react` is fine ŌĆö tree-shaking handles unused icons at build time. Just noting it's a new icon dependency. No action needed.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `AnalysisCostLine`: native branch lacks Popover, unlike Ollama path**

When `allNative` is true, the component returns early with a simple div (no Popover). This differs from the `allOllama` path, which still shows the Popover with per-row breakdown. For native analysis with multiple analysis types (session + prompt_quality + facet = 3 rows), users lose visibility into per-type duration.

This is a design decision, not a bug ŌĆö native sessions don't have meaningful cost data to break down. But if `duration_ms` is tracked per analysis type, a duration breakdown could be useful. Consider whether this is worth adding in a follow-up.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `AnalysisCostLine`: `duration_ms` null coalescing**

```tsx
const totalDurationMs = usage.reduce((s, r) => s + (r.duration_ms ?? 0), 0);
```

This is correct ŌĆö `duration_ms` is `number | null` per the type definition. The `?? 0` fallback is appropriate. However, if ALL rows have `null` duration, the result is `0`, and the display will be `"Analyzed via Claude Code"` without the duration suffix. This is a graceful fallback. Good.

**­¤¤Ī SUGGESTION ŌĆö `AnalysisCostLine`: mixed provider edge case**

```tsx
const allNative = usage.every(row => row.provider === 'claude-code-native');
```

If a session has a mix of native and non-native usage rows (e.g., re-analyzed with a different provider), `allNative` will be false and it falls through to the standard cost path. This is the correct behavior ŌĆö the `allOllama` check has the same semantics. Just confirming the edge case is handled.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö `LlmNudgeBanner`: dismiss state persists even after hook install**

The banner uses `localStorage` to track dismissal. If a user dismisses the banner, then later uninstalls their hook and loses their LLM config, the banner won't reappear (because `dismissed` is read from localStorage before the config check). This is existing behavior, not introduced by this PR ŌĆö the config check on line 42 (`if (llmConfig?.provider) return null`) would hide it anyway when configured. The localStorage dismissal is for users who explicitly don't want to configure. No action needed.

**­¤öĄ NOTE ŌĆö `LlmNudgeBanner`: the `<code>` element for `install-hook` is not copyable**

The `code-insights install-hook` command is displayed in a `<code>` tag but has no copy-to-clipboard affordance. For a terminal command that users need to type, a copy button would improve UX. This is a follow-up enhancement, not a PR blocker.

---

### Verdict

**APPROVE** ŌĆö Clean, focused PR. The LlmNudgeBanner rewrite is well-structured with clear visual hierarchy between the two paths. The AnalysisCostLine native branch correctly follows existing patterns (`allOllama` ŌåÆ `allNative`) and handles edge cases (null duration, mixed providers, legacy guard). No accessibility regressions, no performance concerns, no React anti-patterns.

The suggestions above are all minor follow-up candidates, not blockers. Ship it.
</teammate-message>

# /release ŌĆö Automated Release Workflow

**Arguments**: minor

You are executing the release workflow for `@code-insights/cli`. Parse `minor` to extract:
- **type** (required): `patch`, `minor`, or `major`
- **description** (optional): A one-liner for the release title

If type is missing or not one of `patch`/`minor`/`major`, ask the user to provide it.

---

## Step 1: Pre-flight Checks

Run ALL of these checks. If any fail, STOP and tell the user what to fix.

```bash
# Must be on master
git branch --show-current  # Must output "master"

# Must have clean working tree
git status --porcelain     # Must be empty

# Pull latest
git pull origin master
```

Read the current version from `cli/package.json` (the `"version"` field).

Compute the new version:
- `patch`: increment the third number (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.6.2)
- `minor`: increment the second number, reset third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.7.0)
- `major`: increment the first number, reset second and third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 4.0.0)

**Resume detection**: Run `npm view @code-insights/cli version` to get the currently published version. If the version in `package.json` is ALREADY GREATER than the npm version, this is a **resumed release** ŌĆö skip to Step 6.

---

## Step 2: Analyze Changes

Find the last git tag and analyze what changed:

```bash
# Find latest tag
git describe --tags --abbrev=0

# Commits since last tag
git log $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --oneline

# Full diff since last tag
git diff $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --stat
```

Read the full diff and commit messages. Then:

1. **Generate a CHANGELOG entry** in the existing format (see `cli/CHANGELOG.md` for style). Group changes under `### Added`, `### Changed`, `### Fixed`, `### Improved` as appropriate. Match the existing tone ŌĆö concise but descriptive, with bold lead-ins.

2. **Generate a release title** ŌĆö a short phrase summarizing the release (e.g., "LLM-Powered Export Page", "PostHog custom domain"). Use the user's description if provided, otherwise derive from the changes.

3. **For minor/major releases**: Assess which docs need updating:
   - `docs/ROADMAP.md` ŌĆö if new milestones were completed
   - `docs/PRODUCT.md` ŌĆö if product capabilities changed
   - `docs/VISION.md` ŌĆö for major releases, if the vision expanded
   - `README.md` ŌĆö if user-facing features or setup changed

---

## GATE 1: Review Changelog

**STOP and present to the user:**

```
Release: vX.Y.Z ŌĆö {title}
Type: {patch|minor|major}

Proposed CHANGELOG entry:
ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ
{the generated changelog entry}
ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ

Files to modify:
  - cli/package.json (version bump)
  - cli/CHANGELOG.md (new entry)
  {- docs/ROADMAP.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/PRODUCT.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/VISION.md (if applicable)}

Approve, or tell me what to change?
```

Wait for user approval. If they provide edits, incorporate them.

---

## Step 3: Apply Version Bump

After approval, make the changes:

1. **`cli/package.json`** ŌĆö Update the `"version"` field to the new version
2. **`cli/CHANGELOG.md`** ŌĆö Prepend the new entry at the top (after the header, before the previous version entry). Format: `## [X.Y.Z] - YYYY-MM-DD`
3. **Docs** (if approved at Gate 1) ŌĆö Make the specific updates discussed

---

## Step 4: Build & Test

Run the full build and test suite:

```bash
# Full workspace build (this is what prepublishOnly does)
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights && pnpm build

# Run tests
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights/cli && pnpm test
```

**If build fails ŌåÆ STOP.** Show the error. Do not continue.
**If tests fail ŌåÆ STOP.** Show the error. Do not continue.

---

## GATE 2: Confirm Publish

**STOP and present to the user:**

Show the full `git diff` of all changes made, then:

```
Build: PASSED
Tests: PASSED

Ready to:
  1. Commit changes to master
  2. Push to origin
  3. Publish v{X.Y.Z} to npm
  4. Create GitHub release

Proceed?
```

Wait for explicit user approval before continuing.

---

## Step 5: Commit & Push

Commit with specific files only (never `git add .`):

```bash
# Add only the files we changed
git add cli/package.json cli/CHANGELOG.md
# Add any docs files that were modified (if applicable)
# git add docs/ROADMAP.md docs/PRODUCT.md docs/VISION.md README.md

git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: bump version to vX.Y.Z

{one-line summary of what changed}

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"

git push origin master
```

---

## Step 6: Publish to npm

```bash
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights/cli && npm publish
```

The `prepublishOnly` script in `package.json` handles building all packages and copying dashboard/server dist files automatically.

Verify the publish succeeded:

```bash
npm view @code-insights/cli version
```

If publish fails, show the error and STOP. The commit is already pushed ŌĆö tell the user to fix the issue and re-run `/release` (resume detection will skip to this step).

---

## Step 7: GitHub Release

Create the GitHub release using the changelog entry as the body:

```bash
gh release create vX.Y.Z \
  --title "vX.Y.Z ŌĆö {release title}" \
  --notes "$(cat <<'EOF'
{changelog entry content, formatted for GitHub}

**Full Changelog**: https://github.com/melagiri/code-insights/compare/{previous_tag}...vX.Y.Z
EOF
)"
```

---

## GATE 3: Verify

**STOP and present to the user:**

```
Release vX.Y.Z complete!

  npm: @code-insights/cli@X.Y.Z Ō£ō
  GitHub: {release URL}
  Commit: {commit hash}

Everything look correct?
```

---

## Step 8: Done

Summarize the release:

```
Released @code-insights/cli vX.Y.Z

  Changes: {brief summary}
  npm: https://www.npmjs.com/package/@code-insights/cli
  GitHub: {release URL}
  Files modified: {list}
```

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER skip the gates** ŌĆö always pause for user confirmation
- **NEVER use `git add .` or `git add -A`** ŌĆö add specific files only
- **If build or tests fail, STOP** ŌĆö do not try to fix and continue
- **Commit message format**: `chore: bump version to vX.Y.Z` (matches existing pattern)
- **Resume is safe** ŌĆö if re-run after a partial release, it picks up where it left off

## 1. HowItWorksSection Step 03 ŌĆö Needs Revision

The proposed copy has two problems:

**Problem A: It leads with a segment qualifier.** "Claude Code users:" immediately signals "this might not be for me" to anyone using Cursor, Copilot, or Codex. Step 03 is the payoff moment in a 3-step flow ŌĆö it should feel universally exciting, not conditionally exciting.

**Problem B: The sentence structure is awkward.** Two clauses joined by "Or" reads like a fork in the road, not a step. Steps should feel like forward motion.

**Suggested rewrite:**

```
title: 'Get AI insights automatically'
description: 'Install a hook for zero-config analysis on every session ŌĆö or connect any LLM provider (OpenAI, Gemini, Ollama) for on-demand insights.'
```

This leads with the universal value (automatic insights), mentions the zero-config path without naming a specific tool, and positions the API-key path as an alternative rather than a fallback. The Claude Code specificity belongs on the docs page, not in a 3-step marketing flow.

If you want to call out Claude Code specifically, do it as a small annotation *below* the step description ŌĆö not inline. Something like a `text-muted-foreground text-xs` line: "Claude Code users get this with a single command." But I'd lean toward keeping the step clean and letting the hero or docs carry the tool-specific messaging.

---

## 2. HeroSection ŌĆö Option B, not A or C

**Against A (badge):** The existing badges communicate *product properties* (Local-First, Open Source) and *breadth* (tool names). "Zero-Config Analysis" is a *feature benefit for one tool* ŌĆö it's a different category of information and would feel out of place in that row. Badges should be scannable at a glance; mixing categories breaks that.

**Against C:** Adding both a badge and a text line for the same feature is double-messaging. It signals insecurity about the value prop rather than confidence.

**Option B is correct, with a refinement.** Place it directly below the install command block as a single line in `text-sm text-muted-foreground`:

```
Claude Code users: add install-hook for automatic, zero-cost analysis.
```

Rationale: The install command (`npx @code-insights/cli`) is already the primary CTA. Putting the hook callout *there* catches users at the exact moment they're thinking "what do I do next?" ŌĆö it's contextual, not decorative. Keep it as plain text, not a badge or styled callout. Subtle is right here.

One concern: make sure this line doesn't visually compete with the primary CTA button. It should read as a footnote to the command, not a second call to action.

---

## 3. Docs Page ŌĆö Scope and Placement Feedback

**Placement: Guides, not Getting Started.** "Getting Started" should remain tool-agnostic (install, sync, open dashboard). A tool-specific setup flow is a guide. Route: `/docs/guides/claude-code-setup` is correct.

**Scope concerns:**

- **Step 4 (backfill) is premature in a setup guide.** A user who just installed the hook hasn't ended their first session yet ŌĆö backfill is a power-user action for people with existing history. Move it to a "Tips" or "Next Steps" section at the bottom, clearly separated from the core 3-step flow. The core path should be: install ŌåÆ hook ŌåÆ verify. Done.

- **"Prerequisites" should be minimal.** Don't list "npm/npx available" ŌĆö if someone is using Claude Code, they have Node. Just state "Claude Code installed" and move on. Unnecessary prerequisites make simple things feel complicated.

- **Step 3 (Verify) needs specificity.** "End a session, check dashboard" is vague. What exactly should they see? Specify: "End a Claude Code session. Run `code-insights dashboard`. You should see your session with analysis results (decisions, patterns, learnings) populated." Give them a concrete success signal.

- **Troubleshooting section ŌĆö scope it tightly.** Three items max:
  1. "Hook didn't fire" ŌåÆ check `code-insights config` output, verify hook is listed
  2. "Session shows but no analysis" ŌåÆ check if `claude` CLI is available on PATH (native runner dependency)
  3. "Want to use an API key instead" ŌåÆ link to the LLM configuration guide

More than three and it stops being a getting-started guide and becomes a debugging reference.

**Suggested outline revision:**

```
# Getting Started with Claude Code

## Install Code Insights
npx @code-insights/cli

## Install the Session Hook
code-insights install-hook
(one sentence explaining what this does)

## Verify It Works
1. Start and end a Claude Code session
2. Run: code-insights dashboard
3. Expected: session card shows analysis with decisions, patterns, learnings

## Next Steps
- Backfill existing sessions: code-insights insights check --analyze
- Configure a different LLM provider: [link]
- Explore weekly reflections: code-insights reflect

## Troubleshooting
(3 items as above)
```

---

## 4. UX Concerns

**One real concern: messaging coherence across the three changes.** Right now the plan touches three surfaces (hero, how-it-works, docs) with slightly different framings of the same feature. Make sure the language is consistent:

- Pick ONE phrase and use it everywhere. I'd suggest "zero-config analysis" as the short label and "automatic session analysis via Claude Code hooks" as the full description.
- Don't say "zero-cost" on the marketing site. It's accurate (no API key = no cost), but it implies the alternative *does* cost money, which creates friction for users evaluating the API-key path. "Zero-config" is the better frame ŌĆö it's about convenience, not price.

**No concern about:** the overall feature positioning, the decision to keep it subtle in the hero, or the choice to create a dedicated guide. All three are the right calls.</result>

## TA Plan Review: Landing Page + Docs Updates for v4.8.0 Native Analysis

### Question 1: Web repo conventions

The CLAUDE.md for `code-insights-web` is straightforward. Key conventions to follow:

- **Adding a doc page**: Create the `.mdx` file with frontmatter (`title`, `description`), add to `docsNav` in `docs-nav.ts`, run `pnpm build`. The `generateStaticParams` catch-all route picks it up automatically.
- **Branch discipline**: Feature branch, PR to `master`. Never commit directly to `master`.
- **No environment variables needed** -- pure static export.
- **Frontmatter schema**: `title` (required), `description` (optional). That's it -- no `date`, `tags`, `category`, or other fields. Keep it simple.

No surprises. Your plan aligns with all conventions.

### Question 2: Where should the new page go -- "Getting Started" or "Guides"?

**Recommendation: Guides.**

Here is my reasoning:

- The "Getting Started" section is a three-page linear onramp: Introduction, Installation, Quick Start. It is tool-agnostic and zero-assumption. Adding a Claude Code-specific page here breaks that clean funnel -- a Cursor user would hit a page that doesn't apply to them.
- The "Guides" section is where tool-specific and feature-specific deep dives live. `multi-source.mdx` (tool-specific setup) and `insights-analysis.mdx` (feature deep dive) are both here. A "Getting Started with Claude Code" guide fits this pattern exactly.
- **Placement within Guides**: I would put it right after "Insights & Analysis" and before "Sessions & Chat". The logical flow is: sync sessions, see dashboard, see terminal stats, analyze with LLM (existing), analyze zero-config with Claude Code (new), then explore sessions. Alternatively, placing it right after "Multi-Source Setup" at the end of guides could work since it is source-specific, but the analysis adjacency feels stronger since this is really about the analysis path, not about source setup.

Concrete nav entry:

```typescript
{ title: 'Claude Code Setup', slug: 'guides/claude-code-setup', href: '/docs/guides/claude-code-setup' },
```

Place it after `insights-analysis` in the `docsNav` Guides array.

### Question 3: Frontmatter format

Based on every existing MDX file, the format is:

```yaml
---
title: "Your Title Here"
description: "One sentence description."
---
```

That is the entire frontmatter. `DocsFrontmatter` in `types.ts` only defines `title` (required) and `description` (optional). No date, no category, no tags. Your new file should follow this exact pattern.

One note: `flatNav` is computed from `docsNav` (line 45: `docsNav.flatMap((group) => group.items)`), so you only need to add the entry to `docsNav`. Your plan already noted this correctly.

### Question 4: Architectural concerns

**No blockers. Two minor notes:**

1. **Static generation**: The docs use a `[[...slug]]` catch-all route with `generateStaticParams` that pulls from `flatNav`. Since `flatNav` is derived from `docsNav`, adding the nav entry is sufficient -- no other wiring needed. The MDX file will be compiled at build time by `next-mdx-remote`. No risk here.

2. **HeroSection badge addition**: The existing badge row already has three items (version tag, Local-First, Open Source, and the tool names badge). Adding a fourth "Zero-Config Analysis" badge is fine visually at desktop widths, but at mobile widths (~375px) the flex-wrap row could get crowded with 4-5 badges. Test the mobile layout. If it feels heavy, consider making this a text line below the sub-headline instead of a badge in the badge row. The current badges are identity-level attributes (open source, local-first); "zero-config analysis" is more of a feature callout and may feel out of place alongside them.

3. **HowItWorksSection Step 03 change**: The current copy says "Configure an LLM provider." Your plan changes this to emphasize the hook path for Claude Code users. This is the right call, but be careful with the wording -- this section is tool-agnostic ("One command. No accounts."). The new Step 03 needs to work for all users, not just Claude Code users. I would suggest something like: "Get AI insights automatically" with a description that mentions the hook path first ("Claude Code users get insights automatically via hooks -- no API key needed") and the LLM provider path second ("Or configure any LLM provider for other tools"). This keeps the section universal while highlighting the zero-config path.

### Question 5: Standalone vs. cross-reference to Insights & Analysis

**Cross-reference, not standalone.**

The new Claude Code setup guide should be self-contained for its primary flow (install hook, get analysis automatically), but it should explicitly link to the Insights & Analysis guide for:

- What insight types are extracted (summary, decision, learning, technique, prompt quality) -- don't duplicate those tables
- How prompt quality scoring works -- don't duplicate the dimension/category tables
- Dashboard-based analysis as an alternative path

Think of it like this: the Claude Code Setup guide answers "how do I set this up?" and the Insights & Analysis guide answers "what do I get from it?" The new guide should link to the existing one with a sentence like "For details on what each insight type contains, see [Insights & Analysis](/docs/guides/insights-analysis)."

Also update the Quick Start page (`quick-start.mdx`). Lines 40-46 currently describe the LLM configuration as the only path to insights. Add a mention of the hook path here too, with a link to the new Claude Code guide. Something like:

```
## Get insights automatically (Claude Code)

If you use Claude Code, install the hook for zero-config analysis ŌĆö no API key needed:

\`\`\`bash
code-insights install-hook
\`\`\`

See [Claude Code Setup](/docs/guides/claude-code-setup) for the full guide.
```

This keeps Quick Start as the universal onramp while surfacing the zero-config path early.

## TA Design Review: SessionEnd Hook Cancellation Fix

### Root Cause Confirmation

The diagnosis is correct. `execFileSync('claude', ...)` in `ClaudeNativeRunner` spawns `claude -p` as a **child process of the hook subprocess**. Claude Code's hook manager owns that process tree and terminates it on completion/timeout. Since `claude -p` itself starts a Claude Code session, the hook system kills it. This is a process-tree containment problem, not a timing issue.

### Answers to Your Questions

**1. Process detachment strategy: `nohup ... &` vs `setsid` vs Node `spawn({ detached })`**

Recommendation: **Two-phase approach inside the Node code** (not at the shell level).

- `setsid` is Linux-only (not available on macOS without installing GNU coreutils). Rejected.
- `nohup ... &` at the shell level has the stdin piping problem you identified (question 2). Rejected as the sole approach.
- Node.js `child_process.spawn` with `{ detached: true, stdio: 'ignore' }` combined with `unref()` is the correct approach. It works identically on macOS and Linux. The spawned process gets a new process group (new session leader on Unix), so Claude Code's hook cleanup cannot reach it.

However, you do NOT want to detach `claude -p` itself. You want to detach a **wrapper process** that does: read stdin, sync the file, THEN run `claude -p`. This leads directly to question 3.

**2. Stdin piping concern**

Correct instinct. If you background at the shell level (`&`), stdin delivery is a race condition. The hook process writes stdin, but if the backgrounded child hasn't read it before the parent exits, the pipe breaks.

The fix is: **read stdin synchronously in the foreground hook process, then hand off the parsed data to the detached child.** Stdin must be consumed before any detachment happens.

**3. Architecture: Shell-level vs code-level detachment**

Recommendation: **Code-level detachment, split into two phases.**

The hook command stays as-is (no `nohup`, no `&` in the command string):
```
node /path/code-insights insights --hook --native -q
```

Inside `insightsCommand()` in `insights.ts`, when `opts.hook` is true:

- **Phase 1 (foreground, synchronous):** Read stdin, parse JSON, extract `session_id` and `transcript_path`, run `syncSingleFile()`. This must complete before the hook returns so the session is in the DB.
- **Phase 2 (detached):** Spawn a new Node process that runs the actual analysis: `node /path/code-insights insights <session_id> --native -q`. Use `child_process.spawn` with `{ detached: true, stdio: ['ignore', logFd, logFd] }` and call `child.unref()`. The parent process exits immediately, the hook completes, and the analysis runs in the background.

This is cleaner than shell-level detachment because:
- Stdin is consumed reliably in Phase 1
- The sync completes before the hook returns (data integrity)
- The detached process is a plain `insights <id> --native` call, no hook mode, no stdin dependency
- The hook command string stays simple (no shell escaping concerns with `nohup`/`&`)
- Cross-platform: works on macOS and Linux identically

**4. Error visibility / logging**

Yes, log to `~/.code-insights/hook-analysis.log`. Use append mode. Keep it simple: redirect stdout and stderr of the detached child to that file descriptor.

Open the log file with `fs.openSync(logPath, 'a')`, pass the fd as stdio for the spawned child. This gives you a persistent debug trail without any in-process logging infrastructure.

Add a note in `install-hook` output and/or `code-insights status` that tells users where to find the log. Do not add log rotation yet (YAGNI at current scale).

**5. Race condition: SessionEnd fires before Stop (sync) completes**

This is already handled by the proposed architecture. Phase 1 of the hook command calls `syncSingleFile()` with the `transcript_path` from stdin. This is independent of the Stop hook's full sync. The file is synced to SQLite before the detached analysis starts.

The only remaining race is: what if the session file is still being written when `SessionEnd` fires? This is a Claude Code guarantee question, not ours. `SessionEnd` should only fire after the session file is finalized. If you see truncated data, that is a Claude Code bug, not ours.

No additional mitigation needed here.

**6. Concerns and alternative evaluation**

The proposed approach (Option A with code-level detachment) is the right call. Specific concerns:

- **Option B (pending marker, process later):** Over-engineered. Requires a new table or file-based queue, a polling mechanism or secondary trigger, and adds latency. The analysis should run immediately while the session is fresh. Rejected.

- **Option C (`setsid`):** macOS incompatible. Rejected.

- **Concern: `execFileSync` in the detached process.** The detached child will call `runInsightsCommand()` which uses `ClaudeNativeRunner.execFileSync('claude', ...)`. This `claude -p` will be a grandchild of the detached process, but since the detached process is in its own process group (not under Claude Code's hook tree), the hook manager cannot reach it. This should work. If it does not (belt-and-suspenders), the detached child could also spawn `claude -p` with `{ detached: true }`, but I would not add that unless testing shows it is needed.

- **Concern: Multiple concurrent analyses.** If a user ends sessions rapidly, multiple detached analyses could run simultaneously. Each `claude -p` call is isolated (unique temp files with random suffixes already exist in `native-runner.ts`). SQLite writes use transactions. This is fine.

- **Concern: Hook timeout.** The 300s timeout in the hook config was sized for synchronous analysis. With detachment, Phase 1 (stdin + sync) should complete in under 5 seconds. You could reduce the timeout to 30s, but it is not strictly necessary since the process exits quickly anyway. Leave it at 300s for now to avoid unnecessary churn.

### Implementation Scope

Files to modify:
1. **`cli/src/commands/insights.ts`** ŌĆö Split `insightsCommand()` hook-mode path into Phase 1 (sync) + Phase 2 (detached spawn). The detached child calls `insights <session_id> --native -q` (no `--hook`, passes session ID directly).
2. **`cli/src/commands/install-hook.ts`** ŌĆö No changes needed. The hook command string stays the same.
3. **`cli/src/analysis/native-runner.ts`** ŌĆö No changes needed.

Files to add:
- None. The spawn logic fits naturally in `insights.ts`.

Tests to update:
- Add a test for the detach path in `insights.ts` (mock `child_process.spawn`, verify it is called with `{ detached: true }` and `unref()`).

### Summary

| Decision | Choice | Rationale |
|----------|--------|-----------|
| Detachment mechanism | Node `spawn({ detached: true })` + `unref()` | Cross-platform (macOS + Linux), no shell escaping |
| Detachment level | Code-level, inside `insightsCommand()` | Stdin consumed reliably before detach |
| Phase 1 (foreground) | Read stdin + sync file | Data must be in SQLite before analysis starts |
| Phase 2 (background) | Spawn `insights <id> --native -q` | Clean, no stdin dependency, standard code path |
| Error logging | Append to `~/.code-insights/hook-analysis.log` | Debuggability for background process |
| Hook command string | No change | Keep it simple, detachment is internal |
| Option B (pending marker) | Rejected | Over-engineered, adds latency |
| Option C (setsid) | Rejected | macOS incompatible |

---

**TA Approval:** Approach is aligned with architecture. Proceed with code-level two-phase detachment as described above.</result>
