## Cofounder Design Review: Native Analysis Hook Fix (v4.8.1)

### Severity Assessment

This is a **launch-critical P0**. The flagship v4.8.0 feature -- the one that eliminates the biggest adoption friction (API key requirement) -- is silently broken for 100% of users. The `-q` flag suppresses the error, so there is no feedback at all. Users install the hook, think it is working, and never get insights. This is worse than a visible error; it erodes trust invisibly.

---

### Question 1: User Perception -- Background Execution with No Feedback

**Verdict: Background with no feedback is FINE for the default case. Do NOT add notifications.**

Here is why. The mental model we are selling is "set it and forget it." The hook-powered path is explicitly designed to be invisible infrastructure, not a workflow the user watches. The user's moment of delight is not "analysis finished" -- it is opening the dashboard and seeing insights they did not have to ask for. That is the Spotify Wrapped moment: surprise discovery, not watched progress.

Adding macOS notifications would actually hurt the experience. Developers have notification fatigue. A toast every time a session ends (which could be 10+ times a day for active users) would train them to dismiss it, and they would associate Code Insights with interruption rather than value.

**Precedent:** Obsidian Sync does not notify when sync completes. Git hooks do not notify on success. WakaTime does not notify when it logs time. Successful background infrastructure is silent. Errors are where you surface.

The dashboard already shows a "last analyzed" timestamp on sessions. That is sufficient passive confirmation. If the user cares, they look. If they do not care, we did not interrupt them.

---

### Question 2: Error Handling UX

**Verdict: Option C (let `insights check` catch them), augmented with Option A (log file) for debuggability. Do NOT build Option B yet.**

Reasoning:

- **Option A (log file):** Yes, always. `~/.code-insights/hook-analysis.log` with rotation (last N entries, not unbounded). This is the diagnostic escape hatch for power users and for your own debugging when users file issues. Low cost, high debug value. Every background process needs a log. This is not a feature; it is engineering hygiene.

- **Option B (dashboard notification):** Not yet. Building a "failed analysis" notification system in the dashboard adds complexity (polling, state management, dismissal UX) for a failure case that should be rare once the detach fix works. If analysis failures become common post-fix, then build this. Right now it is speculative infrastructure.

- **Option C (`insights check`):** This already exists and works. It finds unanalyzed sessions and offers to process them. This is your backfill mechanism. A user who runs `code-insights dashboard` or `code-insights stats` will naturally discover unanalyzed sessions through the existing UX. No new code needed.

**The combination:** Log file for debuggability + `insights check` for self-healing. Two mechanisms that already exist or are trivial to add. Zero new dashboard complexity.

**Precedent:** WakaTime logs locally, surfaces errors on next heartbeat check. Sentry SDK logs transport failures locally but does not alert the user.

---

### Question 3: Launch Content Timing

**Verdict: Hold the LinkedIn post. Patch first (v4.8.1), then post. Do NOT pull the marketing site.**

Here is the calculus:

- **The marketing site staying live is fine.** Nobody is browsing code-insights.app right now and rage-testing the hook in the 24-48 hours before the patch ships. The site describes the feature correctly; the feature just needs a patch. Pulling the site and re-deploying creates churn and risks introducing new issues for zero user impact.

- **The LinkedIn post is different.** A post creates a moment in time -- people install immediately, hit the bug, form a first impression. You get exactly one first impression with each person who sees that post. A broken flagship feature on first try is the fastest way to lose a developer permanently. They will not come back for v4.8.1.

- **Ship v4.8.1 within 24-48 hours, then post.** The post does not lose value by waiting two days. The fix (detach the process) is scoped and testable. This is not a multi-week delay.

**If the fix takes longer than expected:** Post with honest framing. "We just shipped native analysis in v4.8.0 -- and immediately found and fixed a hook execution issue in v4.8.1." Developers respect rapid response to bugs more than they respect a perfect launch. But given the fix scope, this should not be necessary.

---

### Question 4: "--- CONVERSATION ---" Clutter Sessions

**Verdict: Filter at sync time. 2 messages or fewer with no tool calls = skip by default.**

This is a data quality issue, not a title generation issue. These are not real sessions -- they are Claude Code's context restoration artifacts. Giving them a better title does not make them useful; it makes clutter look polished.

- **`sync prune` already exists** but requires the user to know about it and run it manually. That violates the zero-config principle. The default experience should not include clutter.

- **Filter at sync time:** Sessions with 2 or fewer messages AND zero tool calls should be skipped during sync. This matches the existing prune heuristic but applies it proactively. Add a `--include-trivial` flag for users who want everything.

- **Do NOT make this part of the v4.8.1 hotfix.** This is a separate quality-of-life improvement. Ship it in v4.9.0 or whatever follows. Do not bundle scope into the critical path fix.

- **Documentation:** Yes, mention `sync prune` in the install-hook output and in the "How it works" section. Low cost, immediately helpful for users who already have clutter.

---

### Question 5: Consolidating Hooks (Remove Stop Hook)

**Verdict: Strongly agree. Ship SessionEnd-only as the default.**

The Stop hook fires on every Claude Code response. For a 30-message session, that is 15+ syncs. Each sync is fast (sub-second), but it is still unnecessary write amplification and it means the database is constantly being written to while the user is working. That is the kind of thing that eventually causes a "why is my disk thrashing?" issue report.

SessionEnd gives you everything you need:
1. Sync the session file (the transcript is complete)
2. Analyze the session (analysis requires the full conversation anyway)

One hook, one trigger, one sync, one analysis. Simpler to explain, simpler to debug, fewer failure modes.

**Migration path:**
- `install-hook` defaults to SessionEnd only (sync + analysis in one command)
- Remove `--sync-only` and `--analysis-only` flags -- they add cognitive load for a split that no longer makes sense
- `uninstall-hook` still cleans up both Stop and SessionEnd hooks (for users who have the old config)
- Existing Stop hooks from v4.8.0 users: `install-hook` should detect and offer to migrate ("Found legacy Stop hook. Replacing with SessionEnd hook.")

**One concern:** Users who want real-time session data in the dashboard while working (seeing messages appear live) would lose that with SessionEnd-only. But this is an edge case, and those users can manually run `code-insights sync` if they want a mid-session update. Do not optimize the default for a power-user edge case.

---

### Question 6: Hook Feedback Messages (SessionStart/SessionEnd)

**Verdict: Cautious yes for SessionStart. No for SessionEnd.**

**SessionStart -- yes, one line:**
A single line at session start is low-friction confirmation that the hook is installed and working. This solves the "is it even doing anything?" anxiety that the current silent behavior creates. The message should be:

```
[Code Insights] Session will be analyzed on end.
```

That is it. No branding flourish, no emoji, no URL. One line that confirms the hook is active and sets the expectation ("on end" -- so they know it is not happening now).

**Why not SessionEnd:** The analysis is happening in the background (per the detach fix). Printing a message at SessionEnd that says "analyzing..." when the process is already detached and the terminal may be closing is unreliable and misleading. The user's next interaction with the results is the dashboard. Let the dashboard be the feedback.

**Implementation note:** This requires adding a SessionStart hook to `install-hook`. Keep it minimal -- just an echo/print command, no Node.js invocation. The lighter the SessionStart hook, the less risk of slowing down session startup.

---

### Overall Recommendation: PROCEED WITH CHANGES

The detach fix (Option A) is the correct approach. It aligns with how every successful background devtool works -- WakaTime, Sentry SDK, Obsidian Sync. The hook should be invisible infrastructure, not a watched process.

**Priority order for the fix:**
1. **v4.8.1 (hotfix, ship in 24-48h):** Detach the analysis process. Add log file. Hold LinkedIn post until this ships.
2. **v4.9.0 (fast follow):** Consolidate to SessionEnd-only. Add SessionStart feedback line. Improve sync-time filtering for trivial sessions. Migrate legacy Stop hooks.

Do not bundle items from bucket 2 into the hotfix. The hotfix has one job: make the flagship feature work.</result>

# /release ŌĆö Automated Release Workflow

**Arguments**: patch

You are executing the release workflow for `@code-insights/cli`. Parse `patch` to extract:
- **type** (required): `patch`, `minor`, or `major`
- **description** (optional): A one-liner for the release title

If type is missing or not one of `patch`/`minor`/`major`, ask the user to provide it.

---

## Step 1: Pre-flight Checks

Run ALL of these checks. If any fail, STOP and tell the user what to fix.

```bash
# Must be on master
git branch --show-current  # Must output "master"

# Must have clean working tree
git status --porcelain     # Must be empty

# Pull latest
git pull origin master
```

Read the current version from `cli/package.json` (the `"version"` field).

Compute the new version:
- `patch`: increment the third number (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.6.2)
- `minor`: increment the second number, reset third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.7.0)
- `major`: increment the first number, reset second and third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 4.0.0)

**Resume detection**: Run `npm view @code-insights/cli version` to get the currently published version. If the version in `package.json` is ALREADY GREATER than the npm version, this is a **resumed release** ŌĆö skip to Step 6.

---

## Step 2: Analyze Changes

Find the last git tag and analyze what changed:

```bash
# Find latest tag
git describe --tags --abbrev=0

# Commits since last tag
git log $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --oneline

# Full diff since last tag
git diff $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --stat
```

Read the full diff and commit messages. Then:

1. **Generate a CHANGELOG entry** in the existing format (see `cli/CHANGELOG.md` for style). Group changes under `### Added`, `### Changed`, `### Fixed`, `### Improved` as appropriate. Match the existing tone ŌĆö concise but descriptive, with bold lead-ins.

2. **Generate a release title** ŌĆö a short phrase summarizing the release (e.g., "LLM-Powered Export Page", "PostHog custom domain"). Use the user's description if provided, otherwise derive from the changes.

3. **For minor/major releases**: Assess which docs need updating:
   - `docs/ROADMAP.md` ŌĆö if new milestones were completed
   - `docs/PRODUCT.md` ŌĆö if product capabilities changed
   - `docs/VISION.md` ŌĆö for major releases, if the vision expanded
   - `README.md` ŌĆö if user-facing features or setup changed

---

## GATE 1: Review Changelog

**STOP and present to the user:**

```
Release: vX.Y.Z ŌĆö {title}
Type: {patch|minor|major}

Proposed CHANGELOG entry:
ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ
{the generated changelog entry}
ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ

Files to modify:
  - cli/package.json (version bump)
  - cli/CHANGELOG.md (new entry)
  {- docs/ROADMAP.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/PRODUCT.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/VISION.md (if applicable)}

Approve, or tell me what to change?
```

Wait for user approval. If they provide edits, incorporate them.

---

## Step 3: Apply Version Bump

After approval, make the changes:

1. **`cli/package.json`** ŌĆö Update the `"version"` field to the new version
2. **`cli/CHANGELOG.md`** ŌĆö Prepend the new entry at the top (after the header, before the previous version entry). Format: `## [X.Y.Z] - YYYY-MM-DD`
3. **Docs** (if approved at Gate 1) ŌĆö Make the specific updates discussed

---

## Step 4: Build & Test

Run the full build and test suite:

```bash
# Full workspace build (this is what prepublishOnly does)
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights && pnpm build

# Run tests
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights/cli && pnpm test
```

**If build fails ŌåÆ STOP.** Show the error. Do not continue.
**If tests fail ŌåÆ STOP.** Show the error. Do not continue.

---

## GATE 2: Confirm Publish

**STOP and present to the user:**

Show the full `git diff` of all changes made, then:

```
Build: PASSED
Tests: PASSED

Ready to:
  1. Commit changes to master
  2. Push to origin
  3. Publish v{X.Y.Z} to npm
  4. Create GitHub release

Proceed?
```

Wait for explicit user approval before continuing.

---

## Step 5: Commit & Push

Commit with specific files only (never `git add .`):

```bash
# Add only the files we changed
git add cli/package.json cli/CHANGELOG.md
# Add any docs files that were modified (if applicable)
# git add docs/ROADMAP.md docs/PRODUCT.md docs/VISION.md README.md

git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: bump version to vX.Y.Z

{one-line summary of what changed}

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"

git push origin master
```

---

## Step 6: Publish to npm

```bash
cd /Users/melagiri/Workspace/codeInsights/code-insights/cli && npm publish
```

The `prepublishOnly` script in `package.json` handles building all packages and copying dashboard/server dist files automatically.

Verify the publish succeeded:

```bash
npm view @code-insights/cli version
```

If publish fails, show the error and STOP. The commit is already pushed ŌĆö tell the user to fix the issue and re-run `/release` (resume detection will skip to this step).

---

## Step 7: GitHub Release

Create the GitHub release using the changelog entry as the body:

```bash
gh release create vX.Y.Z \
  --title "vX.Y.Z ŌĆö {release title}" \
  --notes "$(cat <<'EOF'
{changelog entry content, formatted for GitHub}

**Full Changelog**: https://github.com/melagiri/code-insights/compare/{previous_tag}...vX.Y.Z
EOF
)"
```

---

## GATE 3: Verify

**STOP and present to the user:**

```
Release vX.Y.Z complete!

  npm: @code-insights/cli@X.Y.Z Ō£ō
  GitHub: {release URL}
  Commit: {commit hash}

Everything look correct?
```

---

## Step 8: Done

Summarize the release:

```
Released @code-insights/cli vX.Y.Z

  Changes: {brief summary}
  npm: https://www.npmjs.com/package/@code-insights/cli
  GitHub: {release URL}
  Files modified: {list}
```

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER skip the gates** ŌĆö always pause for user confirmation
- **NEVER use `git add .` or `git add -A`** ŌĆö add specific files only
- **If build or tests fail, STOP** ŌĆö do not try to fix and continue
- **Commit message format**: `chore: bump version to vX.Y.Z` (matches existing pattern)
- **Resume is safe** ŌĆö if re-run after a partial release, it picks up where it left off

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user is the solo developer of Code Insights, an open-source CLI tool for analyzing AI coding sessions. This session covered:
   - Completing Phase 12 (Native Analysis via Claude Code Hooks) v4.8.0 release - dashboard/docs updates, marketing website, and npm publish
   - Testing the hook feature locally and discovering critical bugs
   - Fixing three critical bugs in the hook system (detach execution, infinite loop, fake sessions) and publishing v4.8.1 patch

   - Hold LinkedIn post until hook feature is verified working

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Claude Code Hooks**: `SessionEnd` event fires with `{ session_id, transcript_path, cwd, hook_event_name, reason }` on stdin. `Stop` fires on every response.
   - **`--bare` flag**: Disables OAuth/keychain auth in `claude -p`, forcing `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` only. Removed in PR #255.
   - **Process-tree containment**: Claude Code's hook manager kills child processes. `claude -p` spawned synchronously inside a hook gets "Hook cancelled".
   - **Two-phase detachment**: Phase 1 (foreground): read stdin + sync. Phase 2 (detached): `spawn(process.execPath, args, { detached: true, stdio: ['ignore', logFd, logFd], env: { ...process.env, CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE: '1' } })` + `child.unref()`.
   - **Infinite loop**: `claude -p` ŌåÆ creates session ŌåÆ `SessionEnd` fires ŌåÆ hook triggers ŌåÆ spawns `claude -p` ŌåÆ loop. Broken by `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE` env guard.
   - **`claude -p` session isolation**: `cwd: tmpdir()` in `execFileSync` options prevents `claude -p` from writing JSONL to user's project directory.
   - **Data quality invariant**: `messageCount <= 2` filter exists in `runSync` but was missing from `syncSingleFile`. TA recommended keeping the one-line filter (Option A) rather than extracting a shared function.

3. Files and Code Sections:
   - **`cli/src/commands/insights.ts`** ŌĆö Core insights command, heavily modified across PRs #256, #257
     - Added imports: `spawn` from `child_process`, `openSync/mkdirSync/existsSync` from `fs`, `resolve` from `path`, `fileURLToPath` from `url`, `getConfigDir` from config
     - Added `CLI_ENTRY = resolve(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url), '../../index.js')`
     - Added `HOOK_LOG_PATH = join(getConfigDir(), 'hook-analysis.log')`
     - Hook mode rewritten with env guard + two-phase execution:
       ```typescript
       if (opts.hook) {
         if (process.env.CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE) {
           return; // prevent infinite loop
         }
         // Phase 1: read stdin, sync
         const stdinData = await readStdin();
         // ... parse JSON, syncSingleFile ...
         // Phase 2: detach analysis
         const logFd = openSync(HOOK_LOG_PATH, 'a');
         const args = [CLI_ENTRY, 'insights', resolvedSessionId, '--native', '-q'];
         const child = spawn(process.execPath, args, {
           detached: true,
           stdio: ['ignore', logFd, logFd],
           env: { ...process.env, CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE: '1' },
         });
         child.unref();
         return;
       }
       ```

   - **`cli/src/analysis/native-runner.ts`** ŌĆö ClaudeNativeRunner
     - Removed `--bare` flag from args (PR #255)
     - Changed timeout from `120_000` to `300_000` (PR #255)
     - Added `cwd: tmpdir()` to `execFileSync` options (PR #258)

   - **`cli/src/commands/install-hook.ts`** ŌĆö Hook installation

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **`--bare` blocks subscription auth**: `claude -p --bare` only accepts `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, not OAuth/keychain. Removed `--bare`, increased timeout to 300s.
   - **CI test failures (PR #255)**: Tests asserted `--bare` in args and `120000` timeout. Fixed assertions to match new values.
   - **"Hook cancelled"**: `claude -p` spawned synchronously in hook gets killed by Claude Code. Fixed with detached process spawn.
   - **Infinite hook loop**: Detached `claude -p` creates session ŌåÆ `SessionEnd` fires ŌåÆ hook re-triggers. Burned user's entire usage quota. Fixed with `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE` env var guard.
   - **Fake "--- CONVERSATION ---" sessions**: `claude -p` JSONL files written to user's project dir, picked up by next sync. Fixed with `cwd: tmpdir()` isolation.
   - **`syncSingleFile` missing filter**: Hook-path sync had no Ōēż2 message check. User said "we should call the same function" ŌåÆ TA reviewed ŌåÆ recommended one-line filter (Option A) as correct approach. User approved after TA review.
   - **`sync prune` crash**: `getTrivialSessions()` referenced non-existent `title` column. Fixed to `COALESCE(custom_title, generated_title)`.
   - **CLI_ENTRY path resolution**: Initially used `join()` which doubled the path (`cli/cli/dist/index.js`). Fixed to `resolve()` which correctly traverses up from the file.
   - **Commit to wrong branch**: `getTrivialSessions` fix went to master instead of PR branch. Cherry-picked to PR branch.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` interference**: Users with this env var set will have `claude -p` use API billing instead of subscription. Documented but not programmatically handled.
   - **Testing `claude -p` from within Claude Code**: Not possible ŌĆö hook system interferes. Verified detached spawn works (saw correct PID via `ps aux`) but full e2e requires testing from outside.
   - **Session cb301d97 investigation**: User thought it was fake ŌĆö turned out to be a real session about updating the release skill. Investigation revealed empty messages from tool_result entries being parsed.

# /start-feature ŌĆö Auto-Setup Feature Development Team

**Feature**: Consolidate Stop + SessionEnd hooks into a single SessionEnd hook with SQLite queue-based analysis. Single hook does foreground sync + enqueue, then spawns detached worker (--immediate default). New analysis_queue table (Schema V9). Dashboard shows in-progress state via queue polling. New commands: session-end, queue (status/process/retry/prune). Remove Stop hook and --hook flag from insights. Key decisions: (1) --immediate by default, (2) no auto-process on sync, (3) manual queue prune only (no auto-cleanup). TA plan available via SendMessage to agent a924980c6450872ac.

Key decisions: (1) --immediate by default, (2) no auto-process on sync, (3) manual queue prune only (no auto-cleanup). TA plan available via SendMessage to agent a924980c6450872ac."
}

## Step 3: Spawn PM Agent

The PM agent handles scoping, GitHub Issues, and task graph creation. It does NOT spawn other agents ŌĆö only the orchestrator can spawn agents.

```
Task {
  name: "pm-agent",
  subagent_type: "product-manager",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the PM for this feature team.

WORKTREE: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/
BRANCH: feature/<slugified-arguments>
TEAM: feat-<slugified-arguments>

Your responsibilities are scoping, GitHub Issues, task graph, and handoff preparation.
IMPORTANT: You CANNOT spawn agents. Only the orchestrator can. When you need an agent spawned, message the orchestrator with the request.

Follow this protocol:

1. SCOPE: Read docs in docs/ and CLAUDE.md to understand what this feature involves. Check for existing design docs in docs/plans/. Check docs/architecture/ for architecture context. If the scope is unclear, message the orchestrator for clarification.

2. ISSUES: Search for an existing GitHub Issue that matches this feature. If one exists, use it. If not, create one with proper description, acceptance criteria, and T-shirt size. Record the issue number.

3. TASK GRAPH: Create the ceremony tasks using TaskCreate, then set dependencies with TaskUpdate:
   - Task: 'TA: Review architecture alignment' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if internal-only (new components, UI, styling)
   - Task: 'LLM Expert: Design prompt architecture' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if feature doesn't involve LLM calls
   - Task: 'PM: Prepare handoff context in GitHub Issue' (no dependencies, you do this yourself)
   - Task: 'Dev: Read handoff and design docs, prepare questions' (blockedBy: TA + LLM Expert if applicable + PM handoff)
   - Task: 'Dev + TA: Reach consensus on implementation approach' (blockedBy: above) -- SKIP if internal-only
   - Task: 'Dev: Implement feature in worktree' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Dev: Verify feature and create PR' (blockedBy: above) -- includes pre-PR verification protocol
   - Task: 'Review: Triple-layer code review (loops until 0 FIX NOW)' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Post final review summary to GitHub PR' (blockedBy: above)

4. DO YOUR OWN TASK: Work on your handoff task -- prepare context in the GitHub Issue (description, acceptance criteria, relevant doc paths, implementation guidance).

   IMPORTANT ŌĆö Classify the feature scope for Dev's verification protocol:
   - Does it touch UI/visual rendering? ŌåÆ Tag: VISUAL
   - Does it produce output artifacts (images, PDFs, exports)? ŌåÆ Tag: OUTPUT_ARTIFACT
   - Does it add new npm dependencies? ŌåÆ Tag: NEW_DEPS
   - Does it change API endpoints? ŌåÆ Tag: API_CHANGE
   Include these tags in the GitHub Issue so Dev knows which verification tiers apply.

5. REQUEST AGENT SPAWNS: When your handoff task is done, message the orchestrator:
   - If TA is needed: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: ta-agent ŌĆö [brief context]'
   - When dev prerequisites are met: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: dev-agent ŌĆö [brief context including issue number and key details]'
   The orchestrator will spawn the agents and assign tasks.

   SKIP TA if the feature is internal-only (new components, UI fixes, styling, LLM provider additions). In that case, mark the TA task as completed with note 'Skipped -- internal-only change'.

   If the feature involves LLM calls (prompts, model selection, token budgets, structured output):
   - 'SPAWN_REQUEST: llm-expert-agent ŌĆö [brief context about the LLM aspect]'
   The LLM Expert will design the prompt architecture, token budget, and model recommendation before dev implements.

   SKIP LLM Expert if the feature doesn't touch LLM code. Mark the task as completed with note 'Skipped -- no LLM impact'.

6. MONITOR: Check TaskList periodically.
   - When Dev creates a PR, message the orchestrator: 'REVIEW_REQUEST: PR #XX is ready for /start-review'
   - The orchestrator will run /start-review which loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, the orchestrator sends them to Dev. Dev fixes and pushes. Review re-runs automatically.
   - You do NOT need to request additional review rounds ŌĆö the loop is built into /start-review.

7. REPORT: When review converges (0 FIX NOW items) and final summary is posted, message the orchestrator: 'PR #XX for Consolidate Stop + SessionEnd hooks into a single SessionEnd hook with SQLite queue-based analysis. Single hook does foreground sync + enqueue, then spawns detached worker (--immediate default). New analysis_queue table (Schema V9). Dashboard shows in-progress state via queue polling. New commands: session-end, queue (status/process/retry/prune). Remove Stop hook and --hook flag from insights. Key decisions: (1) --immediate by default, (2) no auto-process on sync, (3) manual queue prune only (no auto-cleanup). TA plan available via SendMessage to agent a924980c6450872ac. is ready for founder review and merge.'

IMPORTANT RULES:
- NEVER merge PRs -- founder-only
- NEVER try to spawn agents -- message the orchestrator instead
- All dev work happens in the worktree
- If you need user clarification, message the orchestrator who will ask the user
- You can message existing teammates directly via SendMessage for routine coordination
- Task dependencies enforce ceremony order -- don't skip steps
- PRE-PR GATE (MANDATORY): Before any PR is created, Dev must complete the full verification protocol (see Dev agent instructions). GitHub Actions costs money ŌĆö failed CI runs are wasted spend.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root ŌĆö must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ ŌĆö must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server ŌĆö do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary
[What this PR does]

## Dependency Audit (if NEW_DEPS)
[Library name]: [Known limitations found, or 'No significant limitations found']

## Verification
- Build: PASS
- Tests: PASS
- [Screenshot of feature rendering] (if VISUAL)
- [Screenshot/proof of output artifact] (if OUTPUT_ARTIFACT)
- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

## During Review Rounds

If the review team sends back FIX NOW items:
1. Read each item carefully
2. Implement the fixes in the worktree
3. Re-run applicable verification tiers (at minimum Tier 1)
4. If fixes are visual, re-capture screenshots
5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable ŌĆö thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

---

## Step 5: Supervise

After spawning agents, your role is active supervisor:

1. **PM handles scoping and task graph** ŌĆö orchestrator handles all agent spawning
2. **Spawn agents when PM sends SPAWN_REQUEST messages**
3. **Intervene when**:
   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user
   - An agent is stuck or reports a blocker -> help unblock
   - PM sends a REVIEW_REQUEST -> run `/start-review` on the PR number
4. **Review loop management**:
   - `/start-review` handles the loop internally (runs rounds until 0 FIX NOW items)
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, relay them to the dev-agent via SendMessage
   - After dev pushes fixes, `/start-review` re-runs targeted reviewers automatically
   - If review hits max rounds (4) without converging, escalate to user
5. **When PM reports "ready for merge"** -> inform the user

---

## Step 6: Cleanup (After PR Merge)

After the founder merges the PR:

1. Send shutdown requests to all teammates (pm-agent, ta-agent, dev-agent)
2. Delete the team: `TeamDelete`
3. Clean up worktree:
```bash
git worktree remove ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>
```
4. Confirm cleanup is complete

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** ŌĆö founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** ŌĆö sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** ŌĆö it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** ŌĆö spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** ŌĆö agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes ŌĆö PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** ŌĆö build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** ŌĆö orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** ŌĆö dev agent must kill any server it starts

<teammate-message teammate_id="pm-agent" color="blue" summary="--hook backward compat decision details">
Here's the exact question for the user:

**Context:** This feature removes the `--hook` flag from `code-insights insights`. But v4.8.x users who ran `install-hook` already have this baked into their `~/.claude/settings.json`:

```
code-insights insights --hook --native -q
```

**Question:** How should we handle those existing users when they upgrade?

**Option A ŌĆö Deprecated alias (recommended):** Keep `--hook` as a silent deprecated alias in `insights` that maps to the new `session-end` behavior. Existing hooks keep working. No user action required. We carry a small shim until v5.

**Option B ŌĆö Auto-upgrade on `install-hook`:** When the user next runs `install-hook`, it detects the old hook in `~/.claude/settings.json` and rewrites it to the new `session-end` command. Cleaner long-term, but modifies user config without an explicit request.

My recommendation is **Option A** ŌĆö it's safer, requires no user action, and the shim is trivial to remove later. But this touches existing user configs so it's the founder's call.
</teammate-message>

## Code Review: PR #261 ŌĆö Hook Queue Consolidation

I reviewed the full diff (22 files, ~900 additions, ~300 deletions). Overall this is a well-structured consolidation. The queue state machine is sound, the migration is safe, and the infinite-recursion guard is correctly placed. Below are my findings.

### FIX NOW (must fix before merge)

#### 1. `installHookCommand()` has no duplicate detection ŌĆö running it twice adds duplicate hooks

**File:** `cli/src/commands/install-hook.ts` (new version in diff)

The old code checked `hookAlreadyInstalled()` before adding. The new code unconditionally pushes:

```js
settings.hooks.SessionEnd.push(newHook);
```

Running `code-insights install-hook` twice will create two identical SessionEnd hooks, causing double sync + double enqueue on every session end. The old `hookAlreadyInstalled()` helper still exists in the file but is no longer called.

**Fix:** Re-add the guard before pushing:
```js
if (hookAlreadyInstalled(settings.hooks.SessionEnd)) {
  console.log(chalk.yellow('Code Insights hook already installed.'));
  console.log(chalk.gray('To reinstall, first run `code-insights uninstall-hook`'));
  return;
}
settings.hooks.SessionEnd.push(newHook);
```

#### 2. `claimNext()` can return the wrong row under concurrent workers

**File:** `cli/src/db/queue.ts`, lines ~80-95

The UPDATE is atomic, but the subsequent SELECT to fetch the claimed row is not part of the same statement:

```js
const result = stmt.run(); // UPDATE ... SET status = 'processing'
if (result.changes === 0) return null;

// This SELECT can return a DIFFERENT row if two workers run concurrently
return db.prepare(
  `SELECT * FROM analysis_queue WHERE status = 'processing' ORDER BY started_at DESC LIMIT 1`
).get() as QueueItem | null;
```

While SQLite's single-writer model prevents truly concurrent UPDATEs within the same database file, there are edge cases: two detached worker processes from rapid session endings could claim different rows, and the `ORDER BY started_at DESC LIMIT 1` query returns whichever was most recent ŌĆö not necessarily the one THIS worker claimed.

**Fix:** Use `RETURNING` clause (SQLite 3.35+, better-sqlite3 supports it):
```js
const row = db.prepare(
  `UPDATE analysis_queue
   SET status = 'processing', started_at = datetime('now')
   WHERE session_id = (
     SELECT session_id FROM analysis_queue
     WHERE status = 'pending'
     ORDER BY enqueued_at ASC
     LIMIT 1
   )
   RETURNING *`
).get() as QueueItem | null;
return row ?? null;
```

Or wrap in a transaction if RETURNING is not desired.

#### 3. `session-end` returns silently on sync failure instead of still enqueuing

**File:** `cli/src/commands/session-end.ts`, lines ~68-76

```js
try {
  await syncSingleFile({ filePath: parsed.transcript_path, sourceTool: options.source, quiet });
} catch {
  if (!quiet) {
    console.error(chalk.yellow('[Code Insights] session-end: sync failed, will retry on next session'));
  }
  return; // <-- exits without enqueuing
}
```

The comment says "will retry on next session" but the session is never enqueued. If sync fails (e.g., transient DB lock), the session is silently dropped from the analysis pipeline. The session data may already be in the DB from a previous sync ŌĆö the analysis could still succeed.

**Fix:** Don't return early. Let it fall through to enqueue + spawn:
```js
} catch {
  if (!quiet) {
    console.error(chalk.yellow('[Code Insights] session-end: sync failed, enqueuing anyway'));
  }
  // Fall through ŌĆö session may already be in DB from a previous sync
}
```

---

### CONSIDER (optional improvements)

#### 4. `useQueuedSessionIds()` creates a new Set on every render

**File:** `dashboard/src/hooks/useAnalysisQueue.ts`, lines ~35-43

`useQueuedSessionIds()` creates a new `Set` object on every call (no `useMemo`). Since it's used in both `SessionListPanel` and `SessionDetailPanel`, each re-render allocates a new Set and triggers downstream re-renders in child components.

**Suggestion:** Wrap in `useMemo`:
```ts
export function useQueuedSessionIds(): Set<string> {
  const { data } = useAnalysisQueue();
  return useMemo(() => {
    if (!data) return new Set();
    return new Set(
      data.items
        .filter(item => item.status === 'pending' || item.status === 'processing')
        .map(item => item.session_id)
    );
  }, [data]);
}
```

#### 5. Hono route mounting order: `/api/analysis/queue` after `/api/analysis` may shadow

**File:** `server/src/index.ts`

The diff adds:
```js
app.route('/api/analysis', analysisRouter);
app.route('/api/analysis/queue', analysisQueueRouter);
```

Hono's `route()` method mounts sub-routers by prefix. If `analysisRouter` has a catch-all or wildcard route, it could intercept `/api/analysis/queue` before the queue router sees it. I checked and the existing `analysisRouter` only has specific routes (`POST /`, `GET /providers`), so this works today ŌĆö but it's fragile.

**Suggestion:** Either mount the more specific route first, or rename to `/api/queue` to avoid prefix overlap.

#### 6. `processQueue` in queue-worker.ts validates `ClaudeNativeRunner` once but items may have mixed `runner_type`

**File:** `cli/src/analysis/queue-worker.ts`, lines ~72-79

The worker creates one `ClaudeNativeRunner` instance and reuses it. But `item.runner_type` is per-item ŌĆö if a user enqueues with `provider` type, the worker passes `_runner: undefined` correctly, but the code path through `runInsightsCommand` with `native: false` will use the provider runner. This works correctly today but the single `validate()` call at the top logs a misleading catch-all if claude CLI is missing (it still processes provider items fine). Minor clarity issue only.

#### 7. `pruneCompleted` SQL string concatenation for days parameter

**File:** `cli/src/db/queue.ts`, line ~191

```js
.run(`-${olderThanDays}`);
```

This constructs the SQLite date modifier string via template literal. While `olderThanDays` comes from `parseInt()` in the commander action (so it's always a number), parameterized queries with string concat for SQLite datetime modifiers are unusual. Not a security issue given the parseInt guard, but worth a comment.

#### 8. No `Loader2` import added to `SessionDetailPanel.tsx` in the diff

The diff adds `<Loader2 className="h-4 w-4 ...">` in SessionDetailPanel but doesn't show an import addition. I verified `Loader2` is already imported in the current file (line 63), so this is fine ŌĆö just noting it for completeness.

---

### Summary

| Category | Count | Items |
|----------|-------|-------|
| FIX NOW | 3 | Duplicate hook detection, claimNext race, sync-failure drops session |
| CONSIDER | 5 | useMemo for Set, route order, mixed runner_type clarity, SQL concat comment, import verification |

The architecture is solid ŌĆö the single SessionEnd hook with SQLite queue is a clear improvement over the two-hook system. The state machine (pending -> processing -> completed/failed) with retry semantics is well-designed. The V9 migration is purely additive and safe. The `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE` recursion guard is correctly propagated through both `session-end` and `native-runner.ts`.

The three FIX NOW items are all straightforward to address and should be resolved before merge.

</teammate-message>

<teammate-message teammate_id="reviewer-round2" color="orange" summary="Round 2 review findings for PR #261">
## Round 2 Review ŌĆö PR #261 (Hook Queue Consolidation)

I've done a thorough review of the final state of the diff. The architecture is clean ŌĆö single SessionEnd hook, SQLite queue with atomic claim, detached worker, dashboard polling. The Round 1 fixes (duplicate hook guard, atomic `claimNext` with RETURNING, sync fall-through) are all properly applied.

Here are my findings:

---

### FIX NOW

**1. File descriptor leak in `spawnWorker()` (`session-end.ts:91-92`)**

`openSync()` returns a numeric fd that is passed to `spawn()` as stdio, but it is never closed in the parent process. After `child.unref()`, the parent should close the fd ŌĆö the child process has inherited its own copy.

```typescript
// Current (leaks fd in parent):
const logFd = openSync(WORKER_LOG_PATH, 'a');
// ... spawn ...
child.unref();

// Should be:
const logFd = openSync(WORKER_LOG_PATH, 'a');
// ... spawn ...
child.unref();
closeSync(logFd);  // import { closeSync } from 'fs'
```

This is called once per session end, so it's a slow leak (one fd per hook invocation until the parent process exits). The parent exits quickly so in practice it doesn't accumulate, but it's still incorrect and could matter if `sessionEndCommand` is ever called in a long-lived process (e.g., tests, or if someone calls it from the server).

**2. `--immediate` flag is accepted but never used (`queue.ts:46-47`)**

`queueProcessCommand` accepts `immediate?: boolean` in its options but never reads or acts on it. The `spawnWorker` in `session-end.ts` passes `--immediate` to the spawned process. Since the flag has no effect, it's dead code that could confuse users who see it in `--help`.

Either remove the flag entirely (since `queue process` already processes everything by default), or document what it's supposed to do differently. If the intent was to skip the stale-reset check or change behavior for worker-spawned invocations, that logic is missing.

---

### CONSIDER

**3. `enqueue()` uses INSERT OR REPLACE ŌĆö resets in-progress analysis**

If a session triggers `SessionEnd` twice in quick succession (e.g., user rapidly ends and restarts), the second `enqueue()` call will `INSERT OR REPLACE` the row, resetting a currently-processing item back to `pending` with `attempt_count = 0`. This silently cancels in-flight analysis.

`INSERT OR IGNORE` might be safer for the "already queued" case, with `INSERT OR REPLACE` reserved for an explicit re-analyze path. Alternatively, the enqueue could check `status != 'processing'` before replacing. The current behavior is documented ("re-enqueuing resets to pending") but the interaction with a concurrent worker deserves consideration.

**4. No query invalidation when background analysis completes**

The dashboard polls `useAnalysisQueue` every 5s and shows "Analyzing..." badges, but when the queue transitions from processing to completed, nothing invalidates the `insights` or `sessions` query keys. The user sees the badge disappear but the actual analysis results won't appear until they navigate away and back (or the next `refetchOnWindowFocus` fires).

Consider: when `useAnalysisQueue` detects that `pending + processing` dropped to 0 (and was previously > 0), invalidate `['insights']` and `['sessions']` so results appear immediately.

**5. `removeStopHooks()` return value logic is subtly fragile (`install-hook.ts:51-54`)**

```typescript
return settings.hooks.Stop === undefined
  ? before > 0
  : settings.hooks.Stop.length < before;
```

After the filter + conditional delete, `settings.hooks.Stop` is either `undefined` (all removed) or a shorter array. The logic works correctly but reads as "was there ever anything?" vs "did we remove something?". A simpler formulation:

```typescript
const after = settings.hooks.Stop?.length ?? 0;
return after < before;
```

This is cosmetic ŌĆö the current code is correct. Just harder to reason about at a glance.

**6. `pruneCompleted()` SQL injection surface via string concatenation (`queue.ts:185`)**

```typescript
.run(`-${olderThanDays}`);
```

The `olderThanDays` parameter comes from `parseInt(opts.days, 10)` in Commander, so it's always a number in practice. But the concatenation pattern (`-${olderThanDays}`) is unusual for parameterized queries. If someone were to call `pruneCompleted()` with a non-numeric value in the future, the string would pass through to SQLite's `datetime()` modifier. This is very low risk given the parseInt guard, but worth noting for code hygiene.

**7. Dashboard polling creates N+1 `useAnalysisQueue` subscriptions**

Both `SessionListPanel` and `SessionDetailPanel` call `useQueuedSessionIds()`, which internally calls `useAnalysisQueue()`. React Query deduplicates the actual fetch (same queryKey), so there's no extra network traffic. But each component creates its own subscription and the `useMemo` in `useQueuedSessionIds` rebuilds the Set independently in each consumer. Not a performance concern at current scale, but if more consumers are added, consider lifting the Set computation into the query's `select` option or a shared context.

---

### Positive Notes

- The atomic `claimNext()` with `UPDATE ... RETURNING *` is well-designed ŌĆö eliminates the timing window that a SELECT-then-UPDATE would have.
- The `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE` env var propagation to `ClaudeNativeRunner` is a smart fix for the recursive hook loop.
- The v4.8.x migration path (removing old Stop hooks, handling both old and new formats in uninstall) is thorough.
- Test coverage for the migration, hook install/uninstall, and resume detection is solid.
- The `markFailed()` retry logic with atomic `attempt_count + 1 >= max_attempts` check is clean.

---

**Summary: 2 FIX NOW, 5 CONSIDER.** The FIX NOWs are the fd leak and the dead `--immediate` flag. Neither is a data-loss risk, but both are code quality issues that should be addressed before merge.
</teammate-message>

# /release ŌĆö Automated Release Workflow

**Arguments**: patch

You are executing the release workflow for `@code-insights/cli`. Parse `patch` to extract:
- **type** (required): `patch`, `minor`, or `major`
- **description** (optional): A one-liner for the release title

If type is missing or not one of `patch`/`minor`/`major`, ask the user to provide it.

---

## Step 1: Pre-flight Checks

Run ALL of these checks. If any fail, STOP and tell the user what to fix.

```bash
# Must be on master
git branch --show-current  # Must output "master"

# Must have clean working tree
git status --porcelain     # Must be empty

# Pull latest
git pull origin master
```

Read the current version from `cli/package.json` (the `"version"` field).

Compute the new version:
- `patch`: increment the third number (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.6.2)
- `minor`: increment the second number, reset third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 3.7.0)
- `major`: increment the first number, reset second and third to 0 (3.6.1 ŌåÆ 4.0.0)

**Resume detection**: Run `npm view @code-insights/cli version` to get the currently published version. If the version in `package.json` is ALREADY GREATER than the npm version, this is a **resumed release** ŌĆö skip to Step 6.

---

## Step 2: Analyze Changes

Find the last git tag and analyze what changed:

```bash
# Find latest tag
git describe --tags --abbrev=0

# Commits since last tag
git log $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --oneline

# Full diff since last tag
git diff $(git describe --tags --abbrev=0)..HEAD --stat
```

Read the full diff and commit messages. Then:

1. **Generate a CHANGELOG entry** in the existing format (see `cli/CHANGELOG.md` for style). Group changes under `### Added`, `### Changed`, `### Fixed`, `### Improved` as appropriate. Match the existing tone ŌĆö concise but descriptive, with bold lead-ins.

2. **Generate a release title** ŌĆö a short phrase summarizing the release (e.g., "LLM-Powered Export Page", "PostHog custom domain"). Use the user's description if provided, otherwise derive from the changes.

3. **For minor/major releases**: Assess which docs need updating:
   - `docs/ROADMAP.md` ŌĆö if new milestones were completed
   - `docs/PRODUCT.md` ŌĆö if product capabilities changed
   - `docs/VISION.md` ŌĆö for major releases, if the vision expanded
   - `README.md` ŌĆö if user-facing features or setup changed

---

**STOP and present to the user:**

```

ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ

ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ

  {- docs/ROADMAP.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/PRODUCT.md (if applicable)}
  {- docs/VISION.md (if applicable)}

Approve, or tell me what to change?
```

Wait for user approval. If they provide edits, incorporate them.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   This session covered three main areas:
   
   **A. Fix: LLM-generated title not applied from CLI path (PR #259)**
   - User discovered that hook-triggered analysis updated the score but not the session title
   - Root cause: `applyGeneratedTitle()` only existed in the server API route, not the CLI insights path
   - User insisted on no duplicate implementations ŌĆö move the function to a shared location
   
   **B. Feature: Hook Queue Consolidation (PR #261)**
   - User wanted to consolidate the noisy Stop hook (fires every Claude response) + SessionEnd hook into a single SessionEnd hook
   - Queue-based analysis system with SQLite `analysis_queue` table (Schema V9)
   - Dashboard should show in-progress analysis state
   - New commands: `session-end`, `queue` (status/process/retry/prune)
   - User decisions: `--immediate` by default, no auto-process on sync, manual queue prune only
   - No backward compatibility needed ("This hook is not released to public yet")
   - Full ceremony via `/start-feature` with PM, TA, Dev, and reviewer agents
   
   **C. Release v4.8.2 (patch)**
   - User explicitly requested patch version (not minor) for both PRs combined
   - Published to npm and GitHub

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **Claude Code Hooks**: `SessionEnd` fires with `{ session_id, transcript_path, cwd, hook_event_name, reason }` on stdin. `Stop` fires on every response (removed in v4.8.2).
   - **Two-phase hook execution**: Phase 1 (foreground) syncs session + enqueues. Phase 2 (detached) spawns worker process.
   - **SQLite analysis queue**: `analysis_queue` table with status state machine (pendingŌåÆprocessingŌåÆcompleted/failed), atomic claim via `UPDATE...RETURNING *`, 3-retry max, stale item reset (>10 min).
   - **Process-tree containment**: Claude Code kills child processes in hooks. Detached spawn with `child.unref()` escapes this.
   - **Infinite loop prevention**: `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE=1` env var guard, now set in both `session-end` spawn AND `native-runner.ts` execFileSync.
   - **`applyGeneratedTitle()`**: Updates `sessions.generated_title` from the summary insight's title. Shared between CLI and server.
   - **Dashboard queue polling**: `useAnalysisQueue` React Query hook polls every 5s when active, 30s when idle. Query invalidation on drain.
   - **Schema V9**: New `analysis_queue` table (additive migration, no existing data affected).
   - **No server required for hooks**: Entire pipeline is CLI ŌåÆ SQLite via better-sqlite3.

3. Files and Code Sections:

   **PR #259 ŌĆö applyGeneratedTitle fix:**
   
   - `cli/src/analysis/analysis-db.ts`
     - Central DB write layer for analysis. Added `applyGeneratedTitle()` function here as the single source of truth.
     - ```typescript
       export function applyGeneratedTitle(sessionId: string, insights: Array<{ type: string; title?: string }>): void {
         const summaryInsight = insights.find(i => i.type === 'summary');
         if (!summaryInsight?.title) return;
         const db = getDb();
         db.prepare('UPDATE sessions SET generated_title = ? WHERE id = ? AND deleted_at IS NULL')
           .run(summaryInsight.title.slice(0, 120), sessionId);
       }
       ```
   
   - `cli/src/commands/insights.ts`
     - Added import of `applyGeneratedTitle` and call after `saveInsightsToDb(sessionInsights)`:
     - ```typescript
       saveInsightsToDb(sessionInsights);
       applyGeneratedTitle(session.id, sessionInsights);
       ```
   
   - `server/src/routes/analysis.ts`
     - Removed local `applyGeneratedTitle` function definition, replaced with import:
     - ```typescript
       import { applyGeneratedTitle } from '@code-insights/cli/analysis/analysis-db';
       ```
   
   **PR #261 ŌĆö Hook Queue Consolidation (22 files, +933/-289):**
   
   - `cli/src/db/queue.ts` (NEW)
     - Queue CRUD: enqueue(), claimNext() with atomic RETURNING *, markCompleted(), markFailed(), resetStale(), getQueueStatus(), pruneCompleted()
   
   - `cli/src/analysis/queue-worker.ts` (NEW)
     - processQueue() loop: claims pending items, runs runInsightsCommand(), handles errors with retry
   
   - `cli/src/commands/session-end.ts` (NEW)
     - Hook entry point: reads stdin JSON, syncSingleFile (non-fatal on failure ŌĆö falls through to enqueue), enqueues, spawns detached worker
     - Closes fd after spawn: `closeSync(logFd)` after `child.unref()`
   
   - `cli/src/commands/queue.ts` (NEW)
     - Subcommands: status, process, retry, prune
   
   - `cli/src/db/migrate.ts` (MODIFIED)
     - Added applyV9() for analysis_queue table with status index
   
   - `cli/src/commands/install-hook.ts` (MODIFIED)
     - Single SessionEnd hook running `session-end` command, removes old Stop hooks
     - `hookAlreadyInstalled()` guard prevents duplicate hooks
   
   - `cli/src/commands/insights.ts` (MODIFIED)
     - `--hook` flag removed entirely. Shows error: "The --hook flag has been removed. Run `code-insights install-hook` to install the updated hook."
     - `hookMode` removed from InsightsCommandOptions
   
   - `cli/src/analysis/native-runner.ts` (MODIFIED)
     - Added `CODE_INSIGHTS_HOOK_ACTIVE: '1'` to execFileSync env options
   
   - `dashboard/src/hooks/useAnalysisQueue.ts` (NEW)
     - React Query hook polling GET /api/analysis/queue every 5s when active, 30s idle
     - `useQueuedSessionIds()` with useMemo for Set construction
     - useRef + useEffect transition detector invalidates ['sessions'] + ['insights'] when queue drains
   
   - `server/src/routes/analysis-queue.ts` (NEW)
     - GET /api/analysis/queue endpoint returning queue items
   
   - Dashboard components (MODIFIED)
